Chapter 1

The people of Israel are apostate, rebellious, and corrupt; only a few remain faithful—The people’s sacrifices and feasts are rejected—They are called upon to repent and work righteousness—Zion will be redeemed in the day of restoration.

1 The [avision](#note1a) of [bIsaiah](#note1b) the son of Amoz, which he saw concerning [cJudah](#note1c) and Jerusalem in the days of [dUzziah](#note1d), [eJotham](#note1e), [fAhaz](#note1f), and Hezekiah, kings of Judah.

2 [aHear](#note2a), O heavens, and give ear, O earth: for the Lord hath spoken, I have nourished and brought up children, and they have [brebelled](#note2b) against me.

3 The ox knoweth his owner, and the ass his master’s [acrib](#note3a): but Israel doth not [bknow](#note3b), my people doth not consider.

4 Ah [asinful](#note4a) nation, a people laden with iniquity, a seed of evildoers, [bchildren](#note4b) that are [ccorrupters](#note4c): they have forsaken the Lord, they have provoked the Holy One of Israel unto [danger](#note4d), they are gone away backward.

5 ¶ Why should ye be [astricken](#note5a) any more? ye will [brevolt](#note5b) more and more: the whole head is sick, and the whole heart [cfaint](#note5c).

6 From the sole of the foot even unto the head there is no soundness in it; but wounds, and bruises, and putrifying sores: they have not been [aclosed](#note6a), neither bound up, neither [bmollified](#note6b) with ointment.

7 Your [acountry](#note7a) is [bdesolate](#note7b), your cities are burned with fire: your land, [cstrangers](#note7c) devour it in your presence, and it is desolate, as overthrown by strangers.

8 And the daughter of Zion is left as a cottage in a [avineyard](#note8a), as [ba](#note8b) lodge in a garden of cucumbers, as a besieged city.

9 Except the Lord of hosts had left unto us a very small [aremnant](#note9a), we should have been as Sodom, and we should have been like unto Gomorrah.

10 ¶ Hear the word of the Lord, ye rulers of [aSodom](#note10a); give ear unto the law of our God, ye people of Gomorrah.

11 To what purpose is the multitude of your [asacrifices](#note11a) unto me? saith the Lord: I am full of the burnt offerings of rams, and the fat of fed beasts; and I [bdelight](#note11b) not in the blood of bullocks, or of lambs, or of he goats.

12 When ye come to appear before me, who hath required this at your hand, to tread my courts?

13 Bring no more [avain](#note13a) [boblations](#note13b); incense is an abomination unto me; the new moons and [csabbaths](#note13c), the calling of [dassemblies](#note13d), I cannot [eaway with](#note13e); it is [finiquity](#note13f), even the [gsolemn meeting](#note13g).

14 Your new [amoons](#note14a) and your appointed [bfeasts](#note14b) my soul hateth: they are a trouble unto me; I am [cweary](#note14c) to bear them.

15 And when ye spread forth your hands, I will hide mine eyes from you: yea, when ye make many [aprayers](#note15a), I will not hear: your hands are full of [bblood](#note15b).

16 ¶ [aWash](#note16a) you, make you [bclean](#note16b); put away the [cevil](#note16c) of your doings from before mine eyes; [dcease](#note16d) to do evil;

17 [aLearn](#note17a) to do [bwell](#note17b); seek [cjudgment](#note17c), [drelieve](#note17d) the oppressed, [ejudge the fatherless](#note17e), plead for the [fwidow](#note17f).

18 Come now, and let us [areason](#note18a) together, saith the Lord: though your [bsins](#note18b) be as scarlet, they shall be as [cwhite](#note18c) as snow; though they be red like crimson, they shall be as wool.

19 If ye be [awilling](#note19a) and [bobedient](#note19b), ye shall eat the [cgood](#note19c) of the land:

20 But if ye refuse and [arebel](#note20a), ye shall be [bdevoured](#note20b) with the sword: for the mouth of the Lord hath spoken it.

21 ¶ How is the faithful city become an [aharlot](#note21a)! it was full of [bjudgment](#note21b); righteousness lodged in it; but now murderers.

22 Thy silver is become [adross](#note22a), thy wine mixed with water:

23 Thy [aprinces](#note23a) are rebellious, and companions of thieves: every one loveth [bgifts](#note23b), and followeth after rewards: they [cjudge not](#note23c) the fatherless, neither doth the cause of the widow come unto them.

24 Therefore saith the Lord, the Lord of hosts, the mighty One of Israel, Ah, I will ease me of mine [aadversaries](#note24a), and avenge me of mine enemies:

25 ¶ And I will [aturn my hand upon](#note25a) thee, and purely [bpurge](#note25b) away thy dross, and take away all thy tin:

26 And I will [arestore](#note26a) thy judges as at the first, and thy [bcounsellors](#note26b) as at the beginning: afterward thou shalt be called, The [ccity of righteousness](#note26c), the faithful city.

27 [aZion](#note27a) shall be redeemed with [bjudgment](#note27b), and her [cconverts](#note27c) with righteousness.

28 ¶ And the destruction of the transgressors and of the sinners shall be together, and they that forsake the Lord shall be consumed.

29 For they shall be ashamed of the [aoaks](#note29a) which ye have desired, and ye shall be confounded for the gardens that ye have chosen.

30 For ye shall be as an oak whose leaf fadeth, and as a garden that hath no water.

31 And the strong shall be [aas tow](#note31a), and the maker of it as a spark, and they shall both [bburn](#note31b) together, and none shall quench them.

Chapter 2

Isaiah sees the latter-day temple, gathering of Israel, and millennial judgment and peace—The proud and wicked will be brought low at the Second Coming—Compare 2 Nephi 12.

1 The word that [aIsaiah](#note1a) the son of Amoz [bsaw](#note1b) concerning Judah and Jerusalem.

2 And it shall come to pass in the [alast days](#note2a), that the [bmountain](#note2b) of the Lord’s [chouse](#note2c) shall be [destablished](#note2d) in the top of the mountains, and shall be exalted above the hills; and all [enations](#note2e) shall flow unto it.

3 And many people shall go and say, Come ye, and let us [ago](#note3a) up to the [bmountain](#note3b) of the Lord, to the [chouse](#note3c) of the God of Jacob; and he will [dteach](#note3d) us of his ways, and we will walk in his paths: for out of [eZion](#note3e) shall go forth the [flaw](#note3f), and the word of the Lord from Jerusalem.

4 And he shall [ajudge](#note4a) among the nations, and shall rebuke many people: and they shall beat their swords into plowshares, and their spears into pruninghooks: nation shall not lift up sword against nation, neither shall they learn [bwar](#note4b) any more.

5 O house of Jacob, come ye, and let us [awalk](#note5a) in the [blight](#note5b) of the Lord.

6 ¶ Therefore thou hast forsaken thy people the house of Jacob, because they [abe](#note6a) replenished from the east, and are [bsoothsayers](#note6b) like the Philistines, and they [cplease themselves in](#note6c) the children of strangers.

7 Their land also is full of silver and gold, neither is there any end of their treasures; their land is also full of horses, neither is there any end of their chariots:

8 Their land also is full of [aidols](#note8a); they [bworship](#note8b) the work of their own hands, that which their own fingers have made:

9 And the [amean man](#note9a) [bboweth](#note9b) down, and the great man humbleth himself: therefore forgive them not.

10 ¶ Enter into the rock, and hide thee in the dust, for fear of the Lord, and for the glory of his majesty.

11 The lofty looks of man shall be humbled, and the haughtiness of men shall be bowed down, and the Lord alone shall be [aexalted](#note11a) in that [bday](#note11b).

12 For the [aday](#note12a) of the Lord of hosts shall be upon every one that is [bproud](#note12b) and lofty, and upon every one that is lifted up; and he shall be brought [clow](#note12c):

13 And upon all the [acedars](#note13a) of Lebanon, that are high and lifted up, and upon all the oaks of Bashan,

14 And upon all the high mountains, and upon all the hills that are lifted up,

15 And upon every high tower, and upon every fenced wall,

16 [aAnd](#note16a) upon all the ships of Tarshish, and upon all pleasant pictures.

17 And the loftiness of man shall be bowed down, and the [ahaughtiness](#note17a) of men shall be made low: and the Lord alone shall be exalted in that day.

18 And the [aidols](#note18a) he shall utterly abolish.

19 And they shall go into the [aholes](#note19a) of the rocks, and into the caves of the earth, for [bfear](#note19b) of the Lord, and for the glory of his majesty, when he ariseth to shake terribly the earth.

20 In that day a man shall [acast](#note20a) his idols of silver, and his idols of gold, which they made each one for himself to worship, to the moles and to the bats;

21 To go into the clefts of the rocks, and into the tops of the ragged rocks, for fear of the Lord, and for the glory of his majesty, when he ariseth to shake terribly the earth.

22 [aCease](#note22a) ye from man, whose breath is in his nostrils: for [bwherein](#note22b) is he to be accounted of?

Chapter 3

Judah and Jerusalem will be punished for their disobedience—The Lord pleads for and judges His people—The daughters of Zion are cursed and tormented for their worldliness—Compare 2 Nephi 13.

1 [aFor](#note1a), behold, the Lord, the Lord of hosts, doth take away from [bJerusalem](#note1b) and from Judah the stay and the staff, the whole stay of [cbread](#note1c), and the whole stay of water,

2 The mighty man, and the man of war, the judge, and the prophet, and the prudent, and the [aancient](#note2a),

3 The captain of fifty, and the honourable man, and the counsellor, and [athe cunning artificer](#note3a), and the [beloquent orator](#note3b).

4 And I will give [achildren](#note4a) to be their princes, and babes shall rule over them.

5 And the people shall be oppressed, every one by another, and every one by his neighbour: the child shall behave himself proudly against the [aancient](#note5a), and the base against the honourable.

6 When a man shall take hold of his brother of the house of his father, saying, Thou hast clothing, be thou our ruler, and let this [aruin](#note6a) be under thy hand:

7 In that day shall he swear, saying, I will not be [aan healer](#note7a); for in my house is neither bread nor clothing: make me not a ruler of the people.

8 For [aJerusalem](#note8a) is ruined, and Judah is [bfallen](#note8b): because their tongue and their doings are against the Lord, to provoke the eyes of his glory.

9 ¶ The shew of their countenance doth witness against them; and they declare their [asin](#note9a) as [bSodom](#note9b), they hide it not. Woe unto their soul! for they have rewarded evil unto themselves.

10 Say ye to the [arighteous](#note10a), that it shall be well with him: for they shall [beat](#note10b) the fruit of their doings.

11 Woe unto the [awicked](#note11a)! it shall be ill with him: for [bthe](#note11b) reward of his hands shall be given him.

12 ¶ As for my people, children are their oppressors, and [awomen](#note12a) rule over them. O my people, they which [blead](#note12b) thee cause thee to err, and destroy the way of thy paths.

13 The Lord standeth up to [aplead](#note13a), and standeth to judge the people.

14 The Lord will enter into [ajudgment](#note14a) with the [bancients](#note14b) of his people, and the [cprinces](#note14c) thereof: for ye have [deaten up](#note14d) the vineyard; the [espoil](#note14e) of the [fpoor](#note14f) is in your houses.

15 What mean ye that ye [abeat](#note15a) my people to pieces, and grind the faces of the poor? saith the Lord God of hosts.

16 ¶ Moreover the Lord saith, Because the [adaughters](#note16a) of Zion are [bhaughty](#note16b), and [cwalk](#note16c) with stretched forth necks and [dwanton](#note16d) eyes, walking and [emincing](#note16e) as they go, and making a tinkling with their feet:

17 Therefore the Lord will smite with a scab the crown of the head of the daughters of Zion, and the Lord will [adiscover their secret parts](#note17a).

18 In that day the Lord will take away the bravery of their tinkling ornaments about their feet, and their [acauls](#note18a), and their [bround](#note18b) tires like the moon,

19 The chains, and the bracelets, and the [amufflers](#note19a),

20 The bonnets, and the ornaments of the legs, and the headbands, and the tablets, and the earrings,

21 The rings, and nose jewels,

22 The [achangeable suits](#note22a) of [bapparel](#note22b), and the mantles, and the wimples, and the crisping pins,

23 The [aglasses](#note23a), and the fine linen, and the hoods, and the veils.

24 And it shall come to pass, that instead of sweet smell there shall be stink; and instead of a girdle [aa rent](#note24a); and instead of well set hair [bbaldness](#note24b); and instead of [ca stomacher](#note24c) a girding of sackcloth; and [dburning](#note24d) instead of [ebeauty](#note24e).

25 Thy [amen](#note25a) shall fall by the sword, and thy mighty in the war.

26 And her [agates](#note26a) shall [blament](#note26b) and [cmourn](#note26c); and she being [ddesolate](#note26d) shall sit upon the [eground](#note26e).

Chapter 4

Zion and her daughters will be redeemed and cleansed in the millennial day—Compare 2 Nephi 14.

1 And in that day [aseven](#note1a) women shall take hold of one [bman](#note1b), saying, We will eat our own bread, and wear our own apparel: only let us be called by thy [cname](#note1c), to take away our [dreproach](#note1d).

2 In that day shall the [abranch](#note2a) of the Lord be [bbeautiful](#note2b) and glorious, and the [cfruit](#note2c) of the earth shall be excellent and comely for them that are [descaped](#note2d) of Israel.

3 And it shall come to pass, that he that is [aleft](#note3a) in [bZion](#note3b), and he that remaineth in [cJerusalem](#note3c), shall be called holy, even every one that is [dwritten among the living](#note3d) in Jerusalem:

4 [aWhen](#note4a) the Lord shall have [bwashed](#note4b) away the filth of the daughters of Zion, and shall have [cpurged](#note4c) the blood of Jerusalem from the midst thereof by the spirit of judgment, and by the spirit of [dburning](#note4d).

5 And the Lord will create upon every dwelling place of mount [aZion](#note5a), and upon her assemblies, a [bcloud](#note5b) and smoke by day, and the shining of a flaming [cfire](#note5c) by night: for upon all the glory shall be a defence.

6 And there shall be a tabernacle for a shadow in the daytime from the heat, and for a place of [arefuge](#note6a), and for a covert from storm and from rain.

Chapter 5

The Lord’s vineyard (Israel) will become desolate, and His people will be scattered—Woes will come upon them in their apostate and scattered state—The Lord will lift an ensign and gather Israel—Compare 2 Nephi 15.

1 [aNow](#note1a) will I [bsing](#note1b) to my wellbeloved a song of my beloved touching his [cvineyard](#note1c). My wellbeloved hath a vineyard [din](#note1d) a very fruitful hill:

2 And he fenced it, and gathered out the stones thereof, and planted it with the choicest vine, and built a tower in the midst of it, and also made a winepress therein: and he looked that it should bring forth grapes, and it brought forth wild grapes.

3 And now, O inhabitants of Jerusalem, and men of Judah, judge, I pray you, betwixt me and my vineyard.

4 What could have been done more to my vineyard, that I have not done in it? wherefore, when I looked that it should bring forth grapes, brought it forth [awild grapes](#note4a)?

5 And now go to; I will tell you what I will do to my [avineyard](#note5a): I will [btake away](#note5b) the hedge thereof, and it shall be eaten up; and break down the [cwall](#note5c) thereof, and it shall be trodden down:

6 And I will lay it waste: it shall not be pruned, nor digged; but there shall come up briers and thorns: I will also command the clouds that they rain no rain upon it.

7 For the [avineyard](#note7a) of the Lord of hosts is the house of Israel, and the men of Judah his pleasant plant: and he looked for [bjudgment](#note7b), but behold oppression; for righteousness, but behold [ca cry](#note7c).

8 ¶ Woe unto them that [ajoin](#note8a) [bhouse to house](#note8b), that lay field to field, till there be no place, that they may [cbe placed alone](#note8c) in the midst of the earth!

9 In mine ears said the Lord of hosts, Of a truth many houses shall be desolate, even great and fair, without inhabitant.

10 Yea, ten acres of vineyard shall yield one [abath](#note10a), and the seed of an homer shall yield an ephah.

11 ¶ Woe unto them that rise up early in the morning, that they may follow strong drink; that continue until night, till [awine](#note11a) inflame them!

12 And the harp, and the [aviol](#note12a), the [btabret](#note12b), and pipe, and wine, are in their feasts: but they [cregard](#note12c) not the [dwork](#note12d) of the Lord, neither consider the operation of his hands.

13 ¶ Therefore my people are gone into [acaptivity](#note13a), because they have no [bknowledge](#note13b): and their honourable men are famished, and their multitude dried up with thirst.

14 Therefore hell hath enlarged herself, and opened her mouth without measure: and their glory, and their multitude, and their [apomp](#note14a), and he that rejoiceth, shall descend into it.

15 And the mean man shall be brought down, and the mighty man shall be humbled, and the eyes of the [alofty](#note15a) shall be humbled:

16 But the Lord of hosts shall be exalted in [ajudgment](#note16a), and God that is [bholy](#note16b) shall be sanctified in righteousness.

17 Then shall the lambs feed after their manner, and the waste places of the fat ones shall strangers eat.

18 Woe unto them that [adraw](#note18a) iniquity with cords of [bvanity](#note18b), and sin [cas](#note18c) it were with a cart rope:

19 That say, [aLet](#note19a) him make [bspeed](#note19b), and [chasten](#note19c) his work, that we may [dsee](#note19d) it: and let the counsel of the Holy One of Israel draw nigh and come, that we may know it!

20 ¶ Woe unto them that call [aevil](#note20a) [bgood](#note20b), and good evil; that put [cdarkness](#note20c) for [dlight](#note20d), and light for darkness; that put bitter for sweet, and sweet for bitter!

21 Woe unto them that are [awise](#note21a) in their own [beyes](#note21b), and [cprudent](#note21c) in their own sight!

22 Woe unto them that are mighty to [adrink](#note22a) [bwine](#note22b), and men of strength to mingle strong drink:

23 Which [ajustify](#note23a) the [bwicked](#note23b) for reward, and [ctake](#note23c) away the righteousness of the righteous from him!

24 Therefore as the fire devoureth the [astubble](#note24a), and the flame consumeth the chaff, so their [broot](#note24b) shall be as rottenness, and their blossom shall go up as dust: because they have cast away the law of the Lord of hosts, and despised the word of the Holy One of Israel.

25 Therefore is the [aanger](#note25a) of the Lord kindled against his people, and he hath [bstretched](#note25b) forth his hand against them, and hath smitten them: and the hills did tremble, and their carcases were torn in the midst of the streets. For all this his anger is not turned away, but his hand is stretched out still.

26 ¶ And he will lift up an [aensign](#note26a) to the nations from far, and will [bhiss](#note26b) unto them from the [cend](#note26c) of the earth: and, behold, they shall [dcome](#note26d) with speed swiftly:

27 None shall be weary nor stumble among them; none shall slumber nor sleep; neither shall the girdle of their loins be loosed, nor the latchet of their shoes be broken:

28 Whose arrows are sharp, and all their bows bent, their horses’ hoofs shall be counted like flint, and their wheels like a whirlwind:

29 Their roaring shall be like a lion, they shall roar like young [alions](#note29a): yea, they shall roar, and lay hold of the [bprey](#note29b), and shall carry it away safe, and none shall deliver it.

30 And in that day they shall roar against them like the roaring of the sea: and if one look unto the land, behold darkness and sorrow, and the [alight](#note30a) is [bdarkened](#note30b) in the heavens thereof.

Chapter 6

Isaiah sees the Lord—His sins are forgiven—He is called to prophesy—He prophesies of the Jews’ rejection of Christ’s teachings—A remnant will return—Compare 2 Nephi 16.

1 [aIn](#note1a) the year that king Uzziah died I [bsaw](#note1b) also the [cLord](#note1c) sitting upon a [dthrone](#note1d), high and lifted up, and [ehis train](#note1e) filled the temple.

2 Above it stood the [aseraphims](#note2a): each one had six wings; with twain he covered his face, and with twain he covered his feet, and with twain he did fly.

3 And one cried unto another, and said, Holy, holy, holy, is the [aLord of hosts](#note3a): the whole earth is full of his [bglory](#note3b).

4 And the [aposts](#note4a) of the door moved at the voice of him that cried, and the house was filled with [bsmoke](#note4b).

5 ¶ Then said I, Woe is me! for I am [aundone](#note5a); because I am a man of [bunclean](#note5b) lips, and I dwell in the midst of a people of unclean lips: for mine eyes have [cseen](#note5c) the [dKing](#note5d), the Lord of hosts.

6 Then flew one of the seraphims unto me, having a live [acoal](#note6a) in his hand, which he had taken with the tongs from off the altar:

7 And he laid it upon my [amouth](#note7a), and said, Lo, this hath touched thy lips; and thine iniquity is [btaken](#note7b) away, and thy sin purged.

8 Also I heard the voice of the Lord, saying, Whom shall I [asend](#note8a), and who will go for us? Then said I, Here am I; [bsend](#note8b) me.

9 ¶ And he said, Go, and tell this people, [aHear](#note9a) ye indeed, but [bunderstand](#note9b) not; and see ye indeed, but [cperceive](#note9c) not.

10 Make the [aheart](#note10a) of this people fat, and make their ears heavy, and [bshut](#note10b) their eyes; lest they see with their eyes, and hear with their ears, and understand with their heart, and convert, and be healed.

11 Then said I, Lord, [ahow](#note11a) long? And he answered, Until the cities be wasted without inhabitant, and the houses without man, and the land be utterly desolate,

12 And the Lord have removed men far away, and there be a great forsaking in the midst of the land.

13 ¶ But yet in it shall be a tenth, and [ait](#note13a) shall return, and shall be eaten: as a teil tree, and as an oak, whose substance is in them, when they cast their leaves: so the holy seed shall be the [bsubstance](#note13b) thereof.

Chapter 7

Ephraim and Syria wage war against Judah—Christ will be born of a virgin—Compare 2 Nephi 17.

1 [aAnd](#note1a) it came to pass in the days of Ahaz the son of Jotham, the son of Uzziah, king of Judah, that [bRezin](#note1b) the [cking](#note1c) of Syria, and [dPekah](#note1d) the son of Remaliah, king of Israel, went up toward Jerusalem to war against it, but could not prevail against it.

2 And it was told the house of David, saying, Syria is confederate with [aEphraim](#note2a). And his heart was moved, and the heart of his people, as the trees of the wood are moved with the wind.

3 Then said the Lord unto Isaiah, Go forth now to meet Ahaz, thou, and [aShear-jashub](#note3a) thy son, at the end of the [bconduit](#note3b) of the upper pool [cin](#note3c) the highway of the fuller’s field;

4 And say unto him, [aTake heed](#note4a), and be quiet; fear not, neither be fainthearted for the two tails of these smoking firebrands, for the fierce anger of Rezin with Syria, and of the son of Remaliah.

5 Because Syria, Ephraim, and the son of Remaliah, have taken evil counsel against thee, saying,

6 Let us go up against Judah, and vex it, and let us [amake a breach](#note6a) therein for us, and set a king in the midst of it, even the son of Tabeal:

7 Thus saith the Lord God, It shall not stand, neither shall it come to pass.

8 For the head of Syria is [aDamascus](#note8a), and the head of Damascus is Rezin; and within threescore and five years shall [bEphraim](#note8b) be broken, that it be not a people.

9 And the head of Ephraim is Samaria, and the head of Samaria is Remaliah’s son. [aIf](#note9a) ye will not believe, surely ye shall not be established.

10 ¶ Moreover the Lord spake again unto Ahaz, saying,

11 Ask thee a sign of the Lord thy God; ask it either in the depth, or in the height above.

12 But Ahaz said, I will not ask, neither will I [atempt](#note12a) the Lord.

13 And he said, Hear ye now, O house of David; Is it a small thing for you to weary men, but will ye weary my God also?

14 Therefore the Lord himself shall give you a [asign](#note14a); [bBehold](#note14b), a [cvirgin](#note14c) shall conceive, and bear a [dson](#note14d), and shall call his name [eImmanuel](#note14e).

15 [aButter and honey](#note15a) shall he eat, that he may know to refuse the evil, and choose the good.

16 For [abefore](#note16a) the child shall know to refuse the [bevil](#note16b), and choose the good, the land that thou abhorrest shall be forsaken of both her kings.

17 ¶ [aThe](#note17a) Lord shall bring upon thee, and upon thy people, and upon thy father’s house, days that have not come, from the day that [bEphraim](#note17b) departed from [cJudah](#note17c); even the king of Assyria.

18 And it shall come to pass in that day, that the Lord shall [ahiss](#note18a) [bfor the fly](#note18b) that is in the uttermost part of the rivers of Egypt, and for the bee that is in the land of Assyria.

19 And they shall come, and shall rest all of them in the desolate valleys, and in the holes of the rocks, and upon all thorns, and upon all bushes.

20 In the same day shall the Lord [ashave](#note20a) with a razor that is hired, namely, by them beyond the river, by the king of Assyria, the head, and the hair of the feet: and it shall also consume the beard.

21 And it shall come to pass in that day, that [aa](#note21a) man shall nourish a young cow, and two sheep;

22 And it shall come to pass, for the abundance of milk that they shall give he shall eat butter: for [abutter and honey](#note22a) shall every one eat that is left in the land.

23 And it shall come to pass in that day, that every place shall be, where there were a thousand vines at a thousand [asilverlings](#note23a), it shall even be for briers and thorns.

24 With arrows and with bows shall men come thither; because all the land shall become briers and thorns.

25 And on all hills that shall be [adigged with the mattock](#note25a), there shall not come thither the fear of briers and thorns: but it shall be for the sending forth of oxen, and for the treading of [blesser cattle](#note25b).

Chapter 8

Christ will be as a stone of stumbling and a rock of offense—Seek the Lord, not muttering wizards—Turn to the law and to the testimony for guidance—Compare 2 Nephi 18.

1 Moreover the Lord said unto me, Take thee a great [aroll](#note1a), and [bwrite](#note1b) in it with [ca man’s pen](#note1c) concerning [dMaher-shalal-hash-baz](#note1d).

2 And I took unto me faithful witnesses to record, Uriah the priest, and Zechariah the son of Jeberechiah.

3 And I went unto [athe prophetess](#note3a); and she conceived, and bare a son. Then said the Lord to me, Call his name [bMaher-shalal-hash-baz](#note3b).

4 For [abefore](#note4a) the child shall [bhave](#note4b) knowledge to cry, My father, and my mother, the riches of Damascus and the spoil of [cSamaria](#note4c) shall be [dtaken](#note4d) away before the king of Assyria.

5 ¶ The Lord spake also unto me again, saying,

6 Forasmuch as this people refuseth the waters of [aShiloah](#note6a) that go softly, and rejoice in [bRezin](#note6b) and Remaliah’s son;

7 Now therefore, behold, the Lord bringeth up upon [athem](#note7a) the [bwaters](#note7b) of the river, strong and many, even the king of [cAssyria](#note7c), and all his glory: and he shall come up over all his channels, and go over all his banks:

8 And he shall [apass through Judah](#note8a); he shall overflow and go over, he shall reach even to the [bneck](#note8b); and the stretching out of his wings shall fill the breadth of thy land, O [cImmanuel](#note8c).

9 ¶ [aAssociate yourselves](#note9a), O ye people, and ye shall be broken in pieces; and give ear, all ye of far countries: gird yourselves, and ye shall be broken in pieces; gird yourselves, and ye shall be broken in pieces.

10 Take [acounsel](#note10a) together, and it shall come to nought; speak the word, and it shall not stand: for [bGod](#note10b) is with us.

11 ¶ For the Lord spake thus to me [awith a strong hand](#note11a), and instructed me that I should not walk in the way of this people, saying,

12 Say ye not, A [aconfederacy](#note12a), to all them to whom this people shall say, A confederacy; neither fear ye their fear, nor be afraid.

13 Sanctify the Lord of hosts himself; and [alet](#note13a) him be your fear, and let him be your dread.

14 And he shall be for a [asanctuary](#note14a); but for a [bstone](#note14b) of [cstumbling](#note14c) and for a [drock](#note14d) of [eoffence](#note14e) to both the houses of Israel, for a gin and for a [fsnare](#note14f) to the inhabitants of Jerusalem.

15 And many among them shall stumble, and fall, and be broken, and be snared, and be taken.

16 [aBind](#note16a) up the testimony, [bseal](#note16b) the [claw](#note16c) among my disciples.

17 And I will wait upon the Lord, that [ahideth](#note17a) his [bface](#note17b) from the house of Jacob, and I will look for him.

18 Behold, I and the children whom the Lord hath given me are for [asigns](#note18a) and for wonders in Israel from the Lord of hosts, which dwelleth in mount Zion.

19 ¶ And when they shall say unto you, Seek unto them that have [afamiliar spirits](#note19a), and unto [bwizards](#note19b) that peep, and that mutter: should not a people seek unto their God? [cfor](#note19c) the living to the dead?

20 To the [alaw](#note20a) and to the testimony: if [bthey](#note20b) speak not according to this word, it is because there is no [clight](#note20c) in them.

21 And [athey](#note21a) shall pass through it, hardly bestead and hungry: and it shall come to pass, that when they shall be hungry, they shall fret themselves, and [bcurse](#note21b) their king and their God, and look upward.

22 And they shall look unto the earth; and behold trouble and [adarkness](#note22a), [bdimness of anguish](#note22b); and they shall be driven to darkness.

Chapter 9

Isaiah speaks about the Messiah—The people in darkness will see a great Light—Unto us a Child is born—He will be the Prince of Peace and reign on David’s throne—Compare 2 Nephi 19.

1 [aNevertheless](#note1a) the dimness shall not be such as was in her vexation, [bwhen](#note1b) at the first he lightly afflicted the land of [cZebulun](#note1c) and the land of Naphtali, and afterward did more grievously afflict her by the way of the sea, beyond Jordan, in Galilee of the nations.

2 The people that walked in [adarkness](#note2a) have seen a great [blight](#note2b): they that dwell in the land of the shadow of death, upon them hath the light shined.

3 Thou hast [amultiplied](#note3a) the [bnation](#note3b), [cand](#note3c) not increased the joy: they joy before thee according to the joy in harvest, and as men [drejoice](#note3d) when they divide the spoil.

4 For thou hast broken the [ayoke](#note4a) of his [bburden](#note4b), and the staff of his shoulder, the [crod](#note4c) of his oppressor, as [din](#note4d) the day of [eMidian](#note4e).

5 [aFor](#note5a) every battle of the warrior is with confused noise, and garments rolled in blood; but this shall be with [bburning](#note5b) and fuel of fire.

6 For unto us a [achild](#note6a) is [bborn](#note6b), unto us a [cson](#note6c) is given: and the [dgovernment](#note6d) shall be upon his shoulder: and his name shall be called Wonderful, [eCounsellor](#note6e), The [fmighty](#note6f) [gGod](#note6g), The [heverlasting](#note6h) Father, The Prince of [iPeace](#note6i).

7 Of the increase of his [agovernment](#note7a) and peace there shall be no [bend](#note7b), upon the throne of [cDavid](#note7c), and upon his kingdom, to order it, and to establish it with judgment and with [djustice](#note7d) from henceforth even for ever. The [ezeal](#note7e) of the Lord of hosts will perform this.

8 ¶ The Lord sent a word into Jacob, and it hath lighted upon [aIsrael](#note8a).

9 And all the people shall know, even Ephraim and the inhabitant of Samaria, that say in the [apride](#note9a) and stoutness of heart,

10 The bricks are fallen down, but we will build with hewn stones: the sycomores are cut down, but we will change them into cedars.

11 Therefore the Lord shall set up the adversaries of [aRezin](#note11a) against him, and join his enemies together;

12 The Syrians [abefore](#note12a), and the Philistines [bbehind](#note12b); and they shall devour Israel with open mouth. For all this his [canger](#note12c) is not turned away, but [dhis](#note12d) hand is [estretched](#note12e) out still.

13 ¶ For the people [aturneth not](#note13a) unto him that smiteth them, neither do they [bseek](#note13b) the Lord of hosts.

14 Therefore the Lord will cut off from Israel head and tail, branch and rush, in one day.

15 The [aancient and honourable](#note15a), he is the head; and the [bprophet](#note15b) that teacheth lies, he is the tail.

16 For the [aleaders](#note16a) of this people cause them to err; and they that are led of them are [bdestroyed](#note16b).

17 Therefore the Lord shall have no joy in their young men, neither shall have mercy on their fatherless and widows: for every one is an [ahypocrite](#note17a) and an evildoer, and every mouth [bspeaketh](#note17b) folly. For all this his anger is not turned away, but his hand is stretched out still.

18 ¶ For wickedness burneth as the fire: it shall devour the briers and [athorns](#note18a), and shall kindle in the [bthickets](#note18b) of the forest, and they shall mount up like the lifting up of smoke.

19 Through the wrath of the Lord of hosts is the land darkened, and the people shall be as the fuel of the fire: no man shall [aspare](#note19a) his [bbrother](#note19b).

20 And he shall snatch on the right hand, and be hungry; and he shall eat on the left hand, and they shall not be satisfied: they shall [aeat](#note20a) every man the [bflesh](#note20b) of his own arm:

21 Manasseh, Ephraim; and Ephraim, Manasseh: and they together shall be against Judah. For all this his anger is not turned away, but his hand is stretched out still.

Chapter 10

The destruction of Assyria is a type of the destruction of the wicked at the Second Coming—Few people will be left after the Lord comes again—The remnant of Jacob will return in that day—Compare 2 Nephi 20.

1 [aWoe](#note1a) unto them that decree [bunrighteous](#note1b) decrees, and that write grievousness which they have prescribed;

2 To turn aside the needy from [ajudgment](#note2a), and to take away the right from the [bpoor](#note2b) of my people, that widows may be their prey, and that they may rob the fatherless!

3 And what will ye do in the day of [avisitation](#note3a), and in the desolation which shall come from far? to whom will ye flee for help? and where will ye leave your glory?

4 Without me they shall bow down under the prisoners, and they shall fall under the slain. For all this his anger is not turned away, but his hand is stretched out still.

5 ¶ O [aAssyrian](#note5a), the rod of mine anger, and the staff in their hand is mine indignation.

6 I will send him against an [ahypocritical](#note6a) nation, and against the people of my wrath will I give him a charge, to take the spoil, and to take the prey, and to tread them down like the mire of the streets.

7 Howbeit he meaneth not so, neither [adoth](#note7a) his heart think so; but it is in his heart to destroy and cut off nations not a few.

8 For he saith, Are not my princes altogether kings?

9 Is not Calno as Carchemish? is not Hamath as Arpad? is not Samaria as Damascus?

10 As my hand hath found the kingdoms of the idols, and whose graven images did excel them of Jerusalem and of Samaria;

11 Shall I not, as I have done unto Samaria and her idols, so do to Jerusalem and her idols?

12 Wherefore it shall come to pass, that when the Lord hath performed his whole work upon mount Zion and on Jerusalem, I will [apunish](#note12a) [bthe fruit](#note12b) of the stout heart of the king of [cAssyria](#note12c), and the glory of his high looks.

13 For he saith, By the [astrength](#note13a) of my hand I have done it, and by my wisdom; for I am prudent: and I have removed the bounds of the people, and have robbed their treasures, and I have put down the inhabitants like a valiant man:

14 And my hand hath found as a nest the riches of the people: and as one gathereth eggs that are left, have I gathered all the earth; and there was none that moved the wing, or opened the mouth, or peeped.

15 [aShall](#note15a) the axe [bboast](#note15b) itself against him that heweth therewith? or shall the saw magnify itself against him that [cshaketh](#note15c) it? as if the rod should shake itself against them that lift it up, or as if the staff should lift up itself, as if it were no wood.

16 Therefore shall the Lord, the Lord of hosts, send among his [afat](#note16a) ones leanness; and under [bhis](#note16b) glory he shall kindle a burning like the burning of a fire.

17 And the light of Israel shall be for a fire, and his Holy One for a flame: and it shall burn and devour his [athorns](#note17a) and his briers in one day;

18 And shall consume the glory of his forest, and of his fruitful field, both [asoul and body](#note18a): and they shall be as when a standardbearer fainteth.

19 And the rest of the trees of his forest shall be few, that a child may write them.

20 ¶ And it shall come to pass in [athat day](#note20a), that the remnant of Israel, and such as are [bescaped](#note20b) of the house of Jacob, shall no more again [cstay upon](#note20c) him that smote them; but shall stay upon the Lord, the Holy One of Israel, in truth.

21 The [aremnant](#note21a) shall [breturn](#note21b), even the remnant of Jacob, unto the mighty God.

22 For though thy people Israel be as the [asand](#note22a) of the sea, yet a remnant of them shall [breturn](#note22b): [cthe](#note22c) [dconsumption](#note22d) [edecreed](#note22e) shall overflow with righteousness.

23 For the Lord God of hosts shall [amake a consumption](#note23a), even determined, in the midst of all the land.

24 ¶ Therefore thus saith the Lord God of hosts, O my people that dwellest in Zion, be not afraid of the Assyrian: he shall [asmite](#note24a) thee with a rod, and shall lift up his staff against thee, after the manner of [bEgypt](#note24b).

25 For yet a very little [awhile](#note25a), and the [bindignation](#note25b) shall cease, and mine anger in their destruction.

26 And the Lord of hosts shall stir up a scourge for him according to the slaughter of [aMidian](#note26a) at the rock of [bOreb](#note26b): and as his [crod](#note26c) was upon the sea, so shall he lift it up after the manner of [dEgypt](#note26d).

27 And it shall come to pass in that day, that his [aburden](#note27a) shall be taken away from off thy shoulder, and his yoke from off thy neck, and the [byoke](#note27b) shall be destroyed because of the [canointing](#note27c).

28 [aHe](#note28a) is come to Aiath, he is passed to Migron; at Michmash he hath laid up his carriages:

29 They are gone over the passage: they have taken up their lodging at Geba; Ramah is afraid; Gibeah of Saul is fled.

30 Lift up thy voice, O daughter of Gallim: cause it to be heard unto Laish, O poor Anathoth.

31 Madmenah is removed; the inhabitants of Gebim gather themselves to flee.

32 As yet shall he remain at Nob that day: he shall shake his hand against the mount of the daughter of Zion, the hill of Jerusalem.

33 Behold, the Lord, the Lord of hosts, shall lop the bough with [aterror](#note33a): and the high ones of stature shall be hewn down, and the [bhaughty](#note33b) shall be humbled.

34 And he shall cut down the [athickets](#note34a) of the forest with iron, and Lebanon shall fall [bby](#note34b) a mighty one.

Chapter 11

The stem of Jesse (Christ) will judge in righteousness—The knowledge about God will cover the earth in the Millennium—The Lord will raise an ensign and gather Israel—Compare 2 Nephi 21.

1 [aAnd](#note1a) there shall come forth a [brod](#note1b) out of the [cstem](#note1c) of [dJesse](#note1d), and a [eBranch](#note1e) shall grow out of his roots:

2 And the [aspirit](#note2a) of the Lord shall rest upon him, the spirit of [bwisdom](#note2b) and [cunderstanding](#note2c), the spirit of [dcounsel](#note2d) and might, the spirit of knowledge and of the fear of the Lord;

3 And shall make him of quick understanding in the fear of the Lord: and he shall not [ajudge](#note3a) [bafter](#note3b) the sight of his eyes, neither reprove after the hearing of his ears:

4 But with righteousness shall [ahe](#note4a) [bjudge](#note4b) the poor, and [creprove with equity](#note4c) for the [dmeek](#note4d) of the earth: and he shall [esmite](#note4e) the earth with the rod of his mouth, and with the [fbreath](#note4f) of his lips shall he [gslay](#note4g) the wicked.

5 And righteousness shall be the [agirdle](#note5a) of his loins, and faithfulness the girdle of his [breins](#note5b).

6 The [awolf](#note6a) also shall dwell with the lamb, and the leopard shall lie down with the kid; and the calf and the young lion and the fatling together; and a little child shall lead them.

7 And the cow and the bear shall feed; their young ones shall lie down together: and the lion shall eat straw like the ox.

8 And the sucking child shall play on the hole of [athe asp](#note8a), and the weaned child shall put his hand on the [bcockatrice’](#note8b) den.

9 They shall not [ahurt](#note9a) nor [bdestroy](#note9b) in all my holy [cmountain](#note9c): for the [dearth](#note9d) shall be full of the [eknowledge](#note9e) of the Lord, as the waters cover the sea.

10 ¶ And in [athat day](#note10a) there shall be a [broot of Jesse](#note10b), which shall stand for an [censign](#note10c) of the people; [dto it](#note10d) shall the [eGentiles](#note10e) seek: and his [frest](#note10f) shall be glorious.

11 And it shall come to pass in that day, that the Lord shall set his hand again the [asecond](#note11a) time to [brecover](#note11b) the [cremnant](#note11c) of his people, which shall be left, from Assyria, and from Egypt, and from Pathros, and from Cush, and from Elam, and from Shinar, and from Hamath, and from the [dislands](#note11d) of the sea.

12 And he shall set up an [aensign](#note12a) for the nations, and shall assemble the outcasts of Israel, and gather together the dispersed of Judah from the four corners of the earth.

13 The envy also of Ephraim shall depart, and the adversaries of Judah shall be cut off: Ephraim shall not [aenvy](#note13a) [bJudah](#note13b), and Judah shall not vex Ephraim.

14 But they shall [afly](#note14a) upon the [bshoulders](#note14b) of the Philistines toward the west; [cthey shall spoil](#note14c) them of the east together: they shall lay their hand upon Edom and Moab; and the children of Ammon shall obey them.

15 And the Lord shall utterly [adestroy](#note15a) the tongue of the [bEgyptian](#note15b) sea; and with his mighty wind shall he shake his hand over the river, and shall smite it in the seven streams, and make men go over dryshod.

16 And there shall be [aan](#note16a) [bhighway](#note16b) for the remnant of his people, which shall be left, from Assyria; like as it was to Israel in the day that he came up out of the land of Egypt.

Chapter 12

In the millennial day, all men will praise the Lord—He will dwell among them—Compare 2 Nephi 22.

1 [aAnd](#note1a) [bin that day](#note1b) thou shalt say, [cO](#note1c) Lord, I will praise thee: though thou wast angry with me, thine anger is turned away, and thou comfortedst me.

2 Behold, God is my salvation; I will trust, and not be afraid: for the Lord [aJehovah](#note2a) is my [bstrength](#note2b) and my song; he also is become my [csalvation](#note2c).

3 Therefore with [ajoy](#note3a) shall ye draw water out of the wells of salvation.

4 And in that day shall ye say, [aPraise](#note4a) the Lord, [bcall upon](#note4b) his name, declare his doings among the people, make mention that his name is exalted.

5 [aSing](#note5a) unto the Lord; for he hath done excellent things: this is known in all the earth.

6 Cry out and shout, thou [ainhabitant](#note6a) of Zion: for great is the Holy One of Israel in the [bmidst](#note6b) of thee.

Chapter 13

The destruction of Babylon is a type of the destruction at the Second Coming—It will be a day of wrath and vengeance—Babylon (the world) will fall forever—Compare 2 Nephi 23.

1 [aThe](#note1a) [bburden](#note1b) of [cBabylon](#note1c), which Isaiah the son of Amoz did see.

2 Lift ye up a [abanner](#note2a) upon the high [bmountain](#note2b), [cexalt](#note2c) the voice unto them, shake the hand, that they may go into the gates of the nobles.

3 I have commanded my [asanctified ones](#note3a), I have also called my [bmighty](#note3b) ones for mine anger, even them that rejoice in my highness.

4 The noise of a multitude in the mountains, like as of a great people; a tumultuous noise of the [akingdoms](#note4a) of nations gathered together: the Lord of hosts mustereth the host of the [bbattle](#note4b).

5 They come from a far country, from the end of heaven, even the Lord, and the weapons of his indignation, to [adestroy](#note5a) the whole land.

6 ¶ [aHowl](#note6a) ye; for the [bday](#note6b) of the Lord is at hand; it shall come as a destruction from the Almighty.

7 Therefore shall all hands be faint, and every man’s heart shall [amelt](#note7a):

8 And they shall be afraid: pangs and sorrows shall take hold of them; they shall be in [apain](#note8a) as a woman that [btravaileth](#note8b): they shall be amazed one at another; their faces shall be as flames.

9 Behold, the day of the Lord cometh, cruel both with wrath and fierce anger, to lay the land desolate: and he shall [adestroy](#note9a) the sinners thereof out of it.

10 For the stars of heaven and the constellations thereof shall not give their light: the sun shall be [adarkened](#note10a) in his going forth, and the moon shall not cause her light to shine.

11 And I will [apunish](#note11a) the [bworld](#note11b) for their evil, and the wicked for their iniquity; and I will cause the arrogancy of the proud to cease, and will lay low the [chaughtiness](#note11c) of the [dterrible](#note11d).

12 I will make a man more [aprecious](#note12a) than fine gold; even a man than the [bgolden](#note12b) wedge of Ophir.

13 Therefore I will [ashake](#note13a) the heavens, and the [bearth](#note13b) shall [cremove](#note13c) out of her place, in the wrath of the Lord of hosts, and in the day of his fierce [danger](#note13d).

14 And it shall be as the [achased roe](#note14a), and as a sheep that [bno man taketh up](#note14b): they shall every man turn to his own [cpeople](#note14c), and flee every one into his own [dland](#note14d).

15 Every one that is found shall be [athrust](#note15a) through; and every one that is joined unto them shall fall by the sword.

16 Their [achildren](#note16a) also shall be dashed to pieces before their eyes; their [bhouses](#note16b) shall be [cspoiled](#note16c), and their wives ravished.

17 Behold, I will stir up the [aMedes](#note17a) against them, which shall not regard silver; and as for gold, they shall not delight in it.

18 Their bows also shall dash the young men to pieces; and they shall have no pity on the fruit of the womb; their eye shall not spare children.

19 ¶ And [aBabylon](#note19a), the glory of kingdoms, the [bbeauty](#note19b) of the [cChaldees’](#note19c) excellency, shall be as when God [doverthrew](#note19d) [eSodom](#note19e) and Gomorrah.

20 It shall never be [ainhabited](#note20a), neither shall it be dwelt in from generation to generation: neither shall the Arabian pitch tent there; neither shall the shepherds make their fold there.

21 But [awild](#note21a) beasts of the desert shall lie there; and their houses shall be full of doleful creatures; and owls shall dwell there, and [bsatyrs](#note21b) shall dance there.

22 And the wild beasts of the islands shall cry in their desolate [ahouses](#note22a), and [bdragons](#note22b) in their pleasant palaces: and her time is near to come, and her days shall not be prolonged.

Chapter 14

Israel will be gathered and enjoy millennial rest—Lucifer was cast out of heaven for rebellion—Israel will triumph over Babylon (the world)—Compare 2 Nephi 24.

1 [aFor](#note1a) the Lord will have [bmercy](#note1b) on Jacob, and will yet [cchoose](#note1c) Israel, and set them in their own [dland](#note1d): and the [estrangers](#note1e) shall be joined with them, and they shall cleave to the house of Jacob.

2 And the [apeople shall take them](#note2a), and [bbring](#note2b) them to their place: and the house of Israel shall possess them in the land of the Lord for servants and handmaids: and they shall take them [ccaptives](#note2c), whose captives they were; and they shall [drule](#note2d) over their oppressors.

3 And it shall come to pass in the day that the Lord shall give thee rest from thy sorrow, and from thy fear, and from the hard bondage wherein thou wast made to serve,

4 ¶ That thou shalt take up this [aproverb](#note4a) against the king of [bBabylon](#note4b), and say, How hath the oppressor ceased! the [cgolden](#note4c) city ceased!

5 The Lord hath broken the [astaff](#note5a) of the [bwicked](#note5b), and the sceptre of the rulers.

6 He who smote the people in wrath with [aa continual stroke](#note6a), he that ruled the nations in anger, is persecuted, and none hindereth.

7 The whole earth is at [arest](#note7a), and is quiet: they break forth into singing.

8 Yea, the [afir trees](#note8a) rejoice at thee, and the cedars of Lebanon, saying, Since thou art [blaid down](#note8b), [cno](#note8c) feller is come up against us.

9 [aHell](#note9a) from beneath is moved for thee to meet thee at thy coming: it stirreth up the [bdead](#note9b) for thee, even all the chief ones of the earth; it hath raised up from their thrones all the kings of the nations.

10 All they shall speak and say unto thee, Art thou also become weak as we? art thou become like unto us?

11 Thy pomp is brought down to [athe grave](#note11a), and the noise of thy viols: the worm is spread under thee, and the worms cover thee.

12 How art thou [afallen](#note12a) from [bheaven](#note12b), O [cLucifer](#note12c), son of the morning! how art thou cut down to the ground, which didst weaken the [dnations](#note12d)!

13 For thou hast said in thine [aheart](#note13a), [bI](#note13b) will ascend into heaven, I will [cexalt](#note13c) my [dthrone](#note13d) above the stars of God: I will sit also upon the mount of the congregation, in the sides of the [enorth](#note13e):

14 I will ascend above the heights of the clouds; I will be like the [amost](#note14a) High.

15 Yet thou shalt be brought down to [ahell](#note15a), to the sides of the pit.

16 They that see [athee](#note16a) shall [bnarrowly look upon thee](#note16b), and consider thee, saying, Is this the man that made the earth to tremble, that did shake kingdoms;

17 That made the world as a wilderness, and destroyed the cities thereof; that opened not the house of his prisoners?

18 All the kings of the nations, even all of them, lie in [aglory](#note18a), every one in [bhis own house](#note18b).

19 But thou art cast out of thy grave like [aan abominable branch](#note19a), and as the raiment of those that are slain, thrust through with a sword, that go down to [bthe stones](#note19b) of the pit; as a carcase trodden under feet.

20 Thou shalt not be [ajoined](#note20a) with them in burial, because thou hast destroyed thy land, and slain thy people: the [bseed](#note20b) of [cevildoers](#note20c) shall never be renowned.

21 [aPrepare](#note21a) slaughter for his children for the iniquity of their fathers; that they do not rise, nor possess the land, nor fill the face of the world with cities.

22 For I will rise up against them, saith the Lord of hosts, and [acut off](#note22a) from Babylon the name, and remnant, and son, and nephew, saith the Lord.

23 I will also make it a possession for the [abittern](#note23a), and pools of water: and I will sweep it with the [bbesom](#note23b) of destruction, saith the Lord of hosts.

24 ¶ The Lord of hosts hath sworn, saying, Surely as I have thought, so shall it come to pass; and as I have purposed, so shall it stand:

25 That [aI](#note25a) will break the Assyrian in my land, and upon [bmy mountains](#note25b) tread him under foot: then shall his [cyoke](#note25c) depart from off them, and his burden depart from off their shoulders.

26 This is the purpose that is purposed upon the whole [aearth](#note26a): and this is the hand that is stretched out upon [ball the nations](#note26b).

27 For the Lord of hosts hath [apurposed](#note27a), and who shall disannul it? and his hand is stretched out, and who shall turn it back?

28 In the [ayear](#note28a) that king [bAhaz](#note28b) died was this [cburden](#note28c).

29 ¶ Rejoice not thou, whole [aPalestina](#note29a), because the rod of him that smote thee is broken: for out of the serpent’s root shall come forth a cockatrice, and his fruit shall be a fiery flying serpent.

30 And the firstborn of the poor shall feed, and the needy shall lie down in safety: and I will kill thy root with famine, and he shall slay thy remnant.

31 [aHowl](#note31a), O gate; cry, O city; thou, whole [bPalestina](#note31b), art dissolved: for there shall come from the north a smoke, and none shall be alone in his appointed times.

32 What shall one then answer the messengers of the [anation](#note32a)? That the Lord hath founded [bZion](#note32b), and the [cpoor](#note32c) of his people shall [dtrust in it](#note32d).

Chapter 15

Moab will be laid waste, and her people will howl and weep.

1 The [aburden](#note1a) of [bMoab](#note1b). Because in the night [cAr](#note1c) of Moab is laid waste, and brought to silence; because in the night Kir of [dMoab](#note1d) is laid waste, and brought to silence;

2 He is gone up to Bajith, and to Dibon, the high places, to weep: Moab shall howl over Nebo, and over Medeba: on all their heads shall be [abaldness](#note2a), and every beard [bcut off](#note2b).

3 In their streets they shall gird themselves with sackcloth: on the tops of their houses, and in their streets, every one shall howl, weeping abundantly.

4 And Heshbon shall [acry](#note4a), and Elealeh: their voice shall be heard even unto Jahaz: therefore the armed soldiers of Moab shall cry out; his life shall be grievous unto him.

5 My [aheart](#note5a) shall cry out for Moab; his fugitives shall flee unto Zoar, an [bheifer](#note5b) of three years old: for by [cthe](#note5c) mounting up of Luhith with weeping shall they go it up; for in the way of [dHoronaim](#note5d) they shall raise up a cry of destruction.

6 For the waters of Nimrim shall be desolate: for the hay is withered away, the grass faileth, there is no green thing.

7 Therefore the abundance they have gotten, and that which they have laid up, shall they carry away to the [abrook of the willows](#note7a).

8 For the cry is gone round about the borders of Moab; the howling thereof unto Eglaim, and the howling thereof unto [aBeer-elim](#note8a).

9 For the waters of Dimon shall be full of blood: for I will bring more upon Dimon, lions upon him that escapeth of Moab, and upon the remnant of the land.

Chapter 16

Moab is condemned, and her people will sorrow—The Messiah will sit on David’s throne, seeking justice and hastening righteousness.

1 [aSend](#note1a) ye the lamb to the ruler of the land from Sela to the wilderness, unto the mount of the daughter of Zion.

2 For it shall be, that, as a wandering bird cast out of the nest, so the daughters of Moab shall be at the fords of [aArnon](#note2a).

3 [aTake counsel](#note3a), execute judgment; make thy shadow as the night in the midst of the noonday; hide the outcasts; bewray not him that wandereth.

4 [aLet](#note4a) mine [boutcasts](#note4b) dwell with thee, Moab; be thou a covert to them from the face of the spoiler: for the extortioner is at an end, the spoiler ceaseth, the oppressors are consumed out of the land.

5 And in [amercy](#note5a) shall the [bthrone](#note5b) be established: and he shall sit upon it in truth in the tabernacle of David, judging, and seeking judgment, and [chasting](#note5c) [drighteousness](#note5d).

6 ¶ [aWe](#note6a) have heard of the [bpride](#note6b) of Moab; he is very proud: even of his haughtiness, and his pride, and his wrath: but his lies shall not be so.

7 Therefore shall Moab [ahowl](#note7a) for Moab, every one shall howl: for the foundations of [bKir-hareseth](#note7b) shall ye mourn; surely they are stricken.

8 For the fields of Heshbon languish, and the vine of Sibmah: the lords of the heathen have broken down the principal plants thereof, they are come even unto [aJazer](#note8a), they wandered through the wilderness: her branches are stretched out, they are gone over the sea.

9 ¶ Therefore I will bewail with the weeping of Jazer the vine of Sibmah: I will water thee with my tears, O Heshbon, and Elealeh: for the shouting for thy summer fruits and for thy harvest is fallen.

10 And [agladness](#note10a) is taken away, and joy out of the plentiful field; and in the vineyards there shall be no singing, neither shall there be shouting: the treaders shall tread out no wine in their presses; I have made their vintage shouting to cease.

11 Wherefore my [abowels](#note11a) shall sound like an harp for Moab, and mine inward parts for Kir-haresh.

12 ¶ And it shall come to pass, when it is seen that Moab is weary on the high place, that he shall come to his sanctuary to [apray](#note12a); but he shall not prevail.

13 This is the word that the Lord hath spoken concerning [aMoab](#note13a) since that time.

14 But now the Lord hath spoken, saying, Within three years, as the years of an hireling, and the glory of Moab shall be contemned, with all that great multitude; and the remnant shall be very small and feeble.

Chapter 17

Israel was scattered because she forgot God—Yet the nations that plunder her will be destroyed.

1 The [aburden](#note1a) of [bDamascus](#note1b). Behold, Damascus is taken away from being a city, and it shall be a ruinous heap.

2 The cities of Aroer are forsaken: they shall be for flocks, which shall lie down, and none shall make them afraid.

3 The fortress also shall cease from [aEphraim](#note3a), and the kingdom from Damascus, and the remnant of Syria: they shall be as the glory of the children of Israel, saith the Lord of hosts.

4 And in that day it shall come to pass, that the glory of Jacob shall be made thin, and the fatness of his flesh shall wax lean.

5 And it shall be as when the harvestman gathereth the corn, and reapeth the ears with his arm; and it shall be as he that gathereth ears in the valley of Rephaim.

6 ¶ Yet [agleaning grapes](#note6a) shall be left in it, as the shaking of an olive tree, two or three berries in the top of the uppermost bough, four or five in the outmost fruitful branches thereof, saith the Lord God of Israel.

7 At that day shall a man look to his [aMaker](#note7a), and [bhis](#note7b) eyes shall have respect to the Holy One of Israel.

8 And he shall not look to the altars, the work of his hands, neither shall respect that which his fingers have made, either the [agroves](#note8a), or the images.

9 ¶ In that day shall his strong cities be as a forsaken bough, and an uppermost branch, which they left because of the children of Israel: and there shall be desolation.

10 Because [athou](#note10a) hast [bforgotten](#note10b) the God of thy [csalvation](#note10c), and hast not been mindful of the [drock](#note10d) of thy strength, therefore [eshalt thou plant](#note10e) pleasant plants, and shalt set it with strange slips:

11 In the day shalt thou make thy plant to grow, and in the morning shalt thou make thy seed to flourish: but the harvest shall be a heap in the day of grief and of desperate sorrow.

12 ¶ Woe to [athe](#note12a) multitude of many people, which make a noise like the noise of the seas; and to the rushing of nations, that make a rushing like the rushing of mighty waters!

13 The nations shall rush like the rushing of many waters: but God shall rebuke them, and they shall flee far off, and shall be chased as the chaff of the mountains before the wind, and like a [arolling](#note13a) thing before the whirlwind.

14 And behold at eveningtide trouble; and before the morning he is not. This is the portion of them that [aspoil](#note14a) us, and the lot of them that rob us.

Chapter 18

The Lord will raise the gospel ensign, send messengers to His scattered people, and gather them to Mount Zion.

1 [aWoe](#note1a) to the land shadowing with wings, which is [bbeyond](#note1b) the rivers of [cEthiopia](#note1c):

2 That sendeth ambassadors by the sea, even in vessels of [abulrushes](#note2a) upon the waters, saying, Go, ye swift messengers, to a nation scattered and peeled, to a people terrible from their beginning hitherto; a nation meted out and trodden down, whose land the rivers have [bspoiled](#note2b)!

3 All ye inhabitants of the world, and dwellers on the earth, see ye, when he lifteth up an [aensign](#note3a) on the mountains; and when he bloweth a trumpet, hear ye.

4 For so the Lord said unto me, I will take my rest, and I will consider in my dwelling place like a clear heat upon herbs, and like a cloud of dew in the heat of harvest.

5 For afore the harvest, when the bud is perfect, and the sour grape is ripening in the flower, he shall both cut off the sprigs with pruning hooks, and take away and cut down the branches.

6 They shall be left together unto the fowls of the mountains, and to the [abeasts](#note6a) of the earth: and the fowls shall summer upon them, and all the beasts of the earth shall winter upon them.

7 ¶ In that time shall the present be brought unto the Lord of hosts of a people [ascattered](#note7a) and peeled, and from a people terrible from their beginning hitherto; a nation meted out and trodden under foot, whose land the rivers have spoiled, to the place of the name of the Lord of hosts, the [bmount Zion](#note7b).

Chapter 19

The Lord will smite and destroy Egypt—Finally He will heal her, and Egypt and Assyria will be blessed with Israel.

1 The [aburden](#note1a) of [bEgypt](#note1b). Behold, the Lord rideth upon a swift [ccloud](#note1c), and shall come into Egypt: and the [didols](#note1d) of Egypt shall be moved at his presence, and the heart of Egypt shall melt in the midst of it.

2 And I will set the Egyptians against the Egyptians: and they shall fight every one against his brother, and every one against his neighbour; city against city, and kingdom against kingdom.

3 And the spirit of Egypt shall fail in the midst thereof; and I will destroy the counsel thereof: and they shall seek to the idols, and to the charmers, and to [athem](#note3a) that have [bfamiliar spirits](#note3b), and to the wizards.

4 And the Egyptians will I give over into the hand of [aa](#note4a) [bcruel](#note4b) lord; and a fierce king shall rule over them, saith the Lord, the Lord of hosts.

5 And the waters shall [afail](#note5a) from the sea, and the river shall be wasted and [bdried](#note5b) up.

6 And they shall turn the rivers far away; and the brooks of defence shall be emptied and dried up: the reeds and flags shall wither.

7 The paper reeds by the brooks, by the mouth of the brooks, and every thing sown by the brooks, shall wither, be driven away, and be no more.

8 The fishers also shall mourn, and all they that cast [aangle](#note8a) into the brooks shall lament, and they that spread nets upon the waters shall languish.

9 Moreover they that work in fine flax, and they that weave [anetworks](#note9a), shall be confounded.

10 And [athey shall be broken](#note10a) in the purposes thereof, all that make sluices and ponds for fish.

11 ¶ Surely the princes of [aZoan](#note11a) are fools, the counsel of the wise counsellors of Pharaoh is become brutish: how say ye unto Pharaoh, I am the son of the wise, the son of ancient kings?

12 Where are they? where are thy wise men? and let them tell thee now, and let them know what the Lord of hosts hath purposed upon Egypt.

13 The princes of Zoan are become fools, the princes of [aNoph](#note13a) are deceived; they have also seduced Egypt, even they that are the [bstay](#note13b) of the tribes thereof.

14 The Lord hath mingled a [aperverse](#note14a) spirit in the midst thereof: and they have caused Egypt to err in every work thereof, as a drunken man staggereth in his vomit.

15 Neither shall there be any work for Egypt, which [athe](#note15a) head or tail, branch or rush, may do.

16 In that day shall [aEgypt](#note16a) be like unto women: and it shall be afraid and fear because of the shaking of the hand of the Lord of hosts, which he shaketh over it.

17 And the land of [aJudah](#note17a) shall be a terror unto Egypt, every one that maketh mention thereof shall be afraid in himself, because of the counsel of the Lord of hosts, which he hath determined against it.

18 ¶ In that day shall five cities in the land of Egypt speak the language of Canaan, and swear to the Lord of hosts; one shall be called, The city of [adestruction](#note18a).

19 In that day shall there be an altar to the Lord in the midst of the land of Egypt, and a pillar at the border thereof to the Lord.

20 And it shall be for a sign and for a witness unto the Lord of hosts in the land of Egypt: for they shall cry unto the Lord because of the oppressors, and he shall send them a saviour, and a great one, and he shall deliver them.

21 And the Lord shall be known to [aEgypt](#note21a), and the Egyptians shall know the Lord in that day, and shall do sacrifice and oblation; yea, they shall vow a [bvow](#note21b) unto the Lord, and perform it.

22 And the Lord shall smite Egypt: he shall smite and heal it: and they shall [areturn](#note22a) even to the Lord, and he shall be entreated of them, and shall heal them.

23 ¶ In that day shall there be a [ahighway](#note23a) out of Egypt to Assyria, and the Assyrian shall come into Egypt, and the Egyptian into Assyria, and the Egyptians shall serve with the Assyrians.

24 In that day shall [aIsrael](#note24a) be the third with Egypt and with Assyria, even a [bblessing](#note24b) in the midst of the land:

25 Whom the Lord of hosts shall bless, saying, Blessed be Egypt my people, and Assyria the work of my hands, and [aIsrael](#note25a) mine [binheritance](#note25b).

Chapter 20

Assyria will overrun Egypt and make her ashamed.

1 In the [ayear](#note1a) that [bTartan](#note1b) came unto Ashdod, (when Sargon the king of Assyria sent him,) and fought against Ashdod, and took it;

2 At the same time spake the Lord by Isaiah the son of Amoz, saying, Go and loose the sackcloth from off thy loins, and put off thy shoe from thy foot. And he did so, walking [anaked](#note2a) and barefoot.

3 And the Lord said, Like as my servant Isaiah hath walked naked and barefoot three years for a [asign](#note3a) and wonder upon Egypt and upon Ethiopia;

4 So shall the [aking](#note4a) of Assyria lead away the Egyptians prisoners, and the [bEthiopians](#note4b) captives, young and old, naked and barefoot, even with their buttocks uncovered, to the shame of Egypt.

5 And [athey](#note5a) shall be afraid and ashamed of Ethiopia their expectation, and of Egypt their glory.

6 And the inhabitant of this isle shall say in that day, Behold, such is our expectation, whither we flee for help to be delivered from the king of Assyria: and how shall we escape?

* [◀](#ldsBACK_note1a)

  1a

  IE about 711 B.C.
* [◀](#ldsBACK_note1b)

  [2 Kgs. 18:17](../2-kgs/18.xhtml#p17).

Chapter 21

Babylon is fallen, is fallen!—Other nations also are destroyed.

1 The [aburden](#note1a) of the desert of the sea. As whirlwinds in [bthe south](#note1b) pass through; so it cometh from the desert, from a terrible land.

2 A grievous vision is declared unto me; the [atreacherous](#note2a) dealer dealeth treacherously, and the spoiler spoileth. Go up, O [bElam](#note2b): besiege, O Media; all the sighing thereof have I made to cease.

3 Therefore are my loins filled with pain: pangs have taken hold upon me, as the pangs of a woman that travaileth: I was bowed down at the hearing of it; I was [adismayed](#note3a) at the seeing of it.

4 My heart panted, fearfulness affrighted me: the night of my pleasure hath he turned into fear unto me.

5 Prepare the table, watch in the watchtower, eat, drink: arise, ye princes, and anoint the shield.

6 For thus hath the Lord said unto me, Go, set a watchman, let him [adeclare](#note6a) what he seeth.

7 And he saw a chariot with a couple of horsemen, a chariot of asses, and a chariot of camels; and he hearkened diligently with much heed:

8 And he cried, A lion: My lord, I stand continually upon the watchtower in the daytime, and I am set in my ward whole nights:

9 And, behold, here cometh a chariot of men, with a couple of horsemen. And he answered and said, [aBabylon](#note9a) is fallen, is fallen; and all the graven images of her gods he hath broken unto the ground.

10 [aO](#note10a) my threshing, and the corn of my floor: that which I have heard of the Lord of hosts, the God of Israel, have I declared unto you.

11 ¶ The [aburden of Dumah](#note11a). He calleth to me out of [bSeir](#note11b), Watchman, [cwhat of the night](#note11c)? Watchman, what of the night?

12 The watchman said, [aThe](#note12a) morning cometh, and also the night: if ye will inquire, inquire ye: return, come.

13 ¶ The [aburden](#note13a) upon Arabia. In the forest in Arabia shall ye lodge, O ye travelling companies of Dedanim.

14 The inhabitants of the land of Tema brought water to him that was thirsty, they prevented with their bread him that fled.

15 For they fled from the swords, from the drawn sword, and from the bent bow, and from the grievousness of war.

16 For thus hath the Lord said unto me, Within a year, according to the years of an hireling, and all the glory of [aKedar](#note16a) shall fail:

17 And the residue of the number of archers, the mighty men of the children of Kedar, shall be diminished: for the Lord God of Israel hath spoken it.

Chapter 22

Jerusalem will be attacked and scourged—The people will be carried captive—The Messiah will hold the key of the house of David, inherit glory, and be fastened as a nail in a sure place.

1 The [aburden](#note1a) of the valley of vision. What aileth thee now, that thou art wholly gone up to the housetops?

2 Thou that art full of [astirs](#note2a), a tumultuous city, a joyous city: thy slain men are not slain with the sword, nor dead in battle.

3 All thy rulers are fled together, they are bound by the archers: all that are found in thee are bound together, which have fled from far.

4 Therefore said I, Look away from me; I will [aweep](#note4a) bitterly, labour not to comfort me, because of the spoiling of the daughter of my people.

5 For it is a day of [atrouble](#note5a), and of treading down, and of perplexity by the Lord God of hosts in the valley of vision, breaking down the walls, and of crying to the mountains.

6 And Elam bare the quiver with chariots of men and horsemen, and Kir uncovered the shield.

7 And it shall come to pass, that thy choicest valleys shall be full of chariots, and the horsemen shall set themselves in array at the gate.

8 ¶ And he [adiscovered](#note8a) the covering of Judah, and thou didst look in that day to the armour of the [bhouse](#note8b) of the forest.

9 Ye have seen also the [abreaches](#note9a) of the city of David, that they are many: and ye gathered together the waters of the lower [bpool](#note9b).

10 And ye have numbered the houses of Jerusalem, and the houses have ye broken down to fortify the wall.

11 Ye made also a [aditch](#note11a) between the two walls for the water of the old pool: but ye have not looked unto the [bmaker](#note11b) thereof, neither had respect unto him that fashioned it long ago.

12 And in that day did the Lord God of hosts [acall](#note12a) to [bweeping](#note12b), and to mourning, and to [cbaldness](#note12c), and to girding with sackcloth:

13 And behold [ajoy](#note13a) and gladness, slaying oxen, and killing sheep, eating flesh, and drinking wine: let us [beat](#note13b) and drink; for [cto morrow](#note13c) we shall die.

14 And it was revealed in mine ears by the Lord of hosts, Surely this iniquity shall not be purged from you till ye die, saith the Lord God of hosts.

15 ¶ Thus saith the Lord God of hosts, Go, get thee unto this treasurer, even unto [aShebna](#note15a), which is over the house, and say,

16 What hast thou here? and whom hast thou here, that thou hast hewed thee out a sepulchre here, as he that heweth him out a sepulchre on high, and that graveth an habitation for himself in a rock?

17 Behold, the Lord will carry thee away with a mighty captivity, and will surely cover thee.

18 He will surely violently turn and toss thee like a ball into a large [acountry](#note18a): there shalt thou die, and there the chariots of thy glory shall be the shame of thy lord’s house.

19 And I will drive thee from thy station, and from thy state shall he pull thee down.

20 ¶ And it shall come to pass in that day, that I will [acall](#note20a) my servant [bEliakim](#note20b) the son of Hilkiah:

21 And I will clothe him with thy robe, and strengthen him with thy girdle, and I will commit thy [agovernment](#note21a) into his hand: and he shall be a father to the inhabitants of Jerusalem, and to the house of Judah.

22 And the [akey](#note22a) of the house of David will I lay upon his shoulder; so he shall open, and none shall shut; and he shall shut, and none shall open.

23 And I will fasten him as a [anail](#note23a) in a sure place; and he shall be for a glorious throne to his father’s house.

24 And they shall hang upon him all the glory of his father’s house, the offspring and the issue, all vessels of small quantity, from the vessels of cups, even to all the vessels of flagons.

25 In that day, saith the Lord of hosts, shall the nail that is fastened in the sure place be removed, and be cut down, and fall; and the burden that was upon it shall be cut off: for the Lord hath spoken it.

Chapter 23

Tyre will be overthrown.

1 The [aburden](#note1a) of [bTyre](#note1b). Howl, ye ships of Tarshish; for it is laid waste, so that there is no house, no entering in: from the land of [cChittim](#note1c) it is revealed to them.

2 Be [astill](#note2a), ye inhabitants of the isle; thou whom the merchants of Zidon, that pass over the sea, have replenished.

3 And by great waters the [aseed](#note3a) of [bSihor](#note3b), the harvest of the river, is her revenue; and she is a mart of nations.

4 Be thou ashamed, O [aZidon](#note4a): for the sea hath spoken, even the [bstrength](#note4b) of the sea, saying, I travail not, nor bring forth children, neither do I nourish up young men, nor bring up virgins.

5 [aAs](#note5a) at the report concerning Egypt, so shall they be sorely pained at the report of Tyre.

6 Pass ye over to Tarshish; howl, ye inhabitants of the isle.

7 Is this your joyous city, whose antiquity is of ancient days? her own feet shall carry her afar off to sojourn.

8 Who hath taken this counsel against Tyre, the crowning city, whose merchants are [aprinces](#note8a), whose [btraffickers](#note8b) are the [chonourable](#note8c) of the earth?

9 The Lord of hosts hath purposed it, to stain the pride of all glory, and to bring into contempt all the honourable of the earth.

10 Pass through thy land as a river, O daughter of Tarshish: there is no more strength.

11 He stretched out his hand over the sea, he shook the kingdoms: the Lord hath given a commandment [aagainst the merchant city](#note11a), to destroy the strong holds thereof.

12 And he said, Thou shalt no more rejoice, O thou oppressed virgin, daughter of Zidon: arise, pass over to Chittim; there also shalt thou have no rest.

13 Behold the land of the [aChaldeans](#note13a); this people was not, till the Assyrian founded it for them that dwell in the wilderness: they set up the towers thereof, they raised up the palaces thereof; and he brought it to ruin.

14 Howl, ye ships of Tarshish: for your strength is laid waste.

15 And it shall come to pass in that day, that Tyre shall be forgotten seventy years, according to the days of one king: after the end of seventy years shall Tyre sing as an harlot.

16 Take an harp, go about the city, thou harlot that hast been forgotten; make sweet melody, sing many songs, that thou mayest be remembered.

17 ¶ And it shall come to pass after the end of seventy years, that the Lord will visit Tyre, and she shall [aturn](#note17a) to her hire, and shall commit [bfornication](#note17b) with all the kingdoms of the world upon the face of the earth.

18 And [aher](#note18a) merchandise and her [bhire](#note18b) shall be [choliness](#note18c) to the Lord: it shall not be treasured nor laid up; for her merchandise shall be for them that dwell before the Lord, to eat sufficiently, and for durable clothing.
