Chapter 44

The Lord’s Spirit will be poured out on the descendants of Israel—Idols of wood are as fuel for a fire—The Lord will gather, bless, and redeem Israel and rebuild Jerusalem.

1 Yet now hear, O Jacob my [aservant](#note1a); and Israel, whom I have chosen:

2 Thus saith the Lord that made thee, and [aformed](#note2a) thee from the womb, which will help thee; Fear not, O Jacob, my servant; and thou, [bJesurun](#note2b), whom I have chosen.

3 For I will pour water upon [ahim](#note3a) that is [bthirsty](#note3b), and floods upon the dry ground: I will pour my [cspirit](#note3c) upon thy seed, and my blessing upon thine offspring:

4 And they shall spring up as among the grass, as willows by the water courses.

5 One shall say, I am the [aLord’s](#note5a); and another shall call himself by the [bname](#note5b) of Jacob; and another shall subscribe with his hand unto the Lord, and surname himself by the name of Israel.

6 Thus saith the Lord the [aKing](#note6a) of Israel, and his redeemer the Lord of hosts; I am the [bfirst](#note6b), and I am the last; and beside me there is no God.

7 And who, as I, shall call, and shall declare it, and set it in order for me, since I appointed the ancient people? and the things that are coming, and shall come, let them shew unto them.

8 [aFear](#note8a) ye not, neither be afraid: have not I told thee from that time, and have declared it? ye are even my witnesses. Is there a God beside me? yea, there is no [bGod](#note8b); I know not any.

9 ¶ They that make a graven [aimage](#note9a) are all of them vanity; and their [bdelectable things](#note9b) shall not profit; and they are their own witnesses; they [csee not](#note9c), nor know; that they may be ashamed.

10 Who hath formed a god, or molten a graven [aimage](#note10a) that is profitable for nothing?

11 Behold, all his [afellows](#note11a) shall be ashamed: and the workmen, they are of men: let them all be gathered together, let them stand up; yet they shall fear, and they shall be ashamed together.

12 The [asmith](#note12a) with the tongs both worketh in the coals, and fashioneth it with hammers, and worketh it with the strength of his arms: yea, he is hungry, and his strength faileth: he drinketh no water, and is faint.

13 The carpenter stretcheth out his rule; he marketh it out with a line; he fitteth it with planes, and he marketh it out with the compass, and maketh it after the figure of a man, according to the beauty of a man; that it may remain in the house.

14 He heweth him down cedars, and taketh the cypress and the oak, which he strengtheneth for himself among the trees of the forest: he planteth an ash, and the rain doth nourish it.

15 Then shall it be for a man to burn: for he will take thereof, and warm himself; yea, he kindleth it, and baketh bread; yea, he maketh a god, and worshippeth it; he maketh it a graven image, and falleth down thereto.

16 He burneth part thereof in the fire; with part thereof he eateth flesh; he roasteth roast, and is satisfied: yea, he warmeth himself, and saith, Aha, I am warm, I have seen the fire:

17 And the residue thereof he maketh a god, even his graven image: he falleth down unto it, and worshippeth it, and prayeth unto it, and saith, Deliver me; for thou art my god.

18 They have not [aknown](#note18a) nor understood: for he hath [bshut](#note18b) their eyes, that they cannot see; and their [chearts](#note18c), that they cannot understand.

19 And none considereth in his heart, neither is there knowledge nor understanding to say, I have burned part of it in the fire; yea, also I have baked bread upon the coals thereof; I have roasted flesh, and eaten it: and shall I make the residue thereof an abomination? shall I fall down to the [astock](#note19a) of a tree?

20 He feedeth on ashes: a [adeceived](#note20a) heart hath turned him aside, that he cannot deliver his soul, nor say, Is there not a [blie](#note20b) in my right hand?

21 ¶ Remember [athese](#note21a), O Jacob and Israel; for thou art my [bservant](#note21b): I have formed thee; thou art my servant: O Israel, thou shalt not be [cforgotten](#note21c) of me.

22 I have blotted out, as a thick cloud, thy [atransgressions](#note22a), and, as a cloud, thy sins: return unto me; for I have redeemed thee.

23 [aSing](#note23a), O ye heavens; for the Lord hath done it: shout, ye lower parts of the earth: break forth into [bsinging](#note23b), ye mountains, O forest, and every tree therein: for the Lord hath [credeemed](#note23c) Jacob, and glorified himself in Israel.

24 Thus saith the Lord, thy [aredeemer](#note24a), and he that [bformed](#note24b) thee from the womb, I am the Lord that [cmaketh](#note24c) all things; that stretcheth forth the heavens alone; that spreadeth abroad the earth by myself;

25 That frustrateth the tokens of the liars, and maketh diviners mad; that turneth [awise](#note25a) men backward, and maketh their knowledge foolish;

26 That confirmeth the word of his servant, and performeth the counsel of his messengers; that saith to Jerusalem, Thou shalt be inhabited; and to the cities of Judah, Ye shall be built, and I will raise up the decayed places thereof:

27 That saith to the deep, Be dry, and I will [adry up](#note27a) thy rivers:

28 That saith of [aCyrus](#note28a), He is my [bshepherd](#note28b), and shall perform all my [cpleasure](#note28c): even saying to Jerusalem, Thou shalt be [dbuilt](#note28d); and to the [etemple](#note28e), Thy foundation shall be laid.

Chapter 45

Cyrus will free the captives of Israel from Babylon—Come unto Jehovah (Christ) and be saved—To Him every knee will bow and every tongue will take an oath.

1 Thus saith the Lord to his [aanointed](#note1a), to [bCyrus](#note1b), whose right hand I have [cholden](#note1c), to [dsubdue](#note1d) nations before him; and I will loose the loins of kings, to open before him the [etwo leaved gates](#note1e); and the gates shall not be shut;

2 I will go before thee, and make the [acrooked](#note2a) places straight: I will [bbreak](#note2b) in pieces the gates of brass, and cut in sunder the bars of iron:

3 And I will give thee the [atreasures of darkness](#note3a), and hidden riches of secret places, that thou mayest know that I, the Lord, which call thee by thy [bname](#note3b), am the [cGod](#note3c) of Israel.

4 For Jacob my [aservant’s](#note4a) sake, and Israel mine [belect](#note4b), I have even [ccalled](#note4c) thee by thy name: I have surnamed thee, though thou hast not known me.

5 ¶ [aI am](#note5a) the Lord, and there is none else, there is no God beside me: I girded thee, though thou hast not known me:

6 That they may know from the [arising](#note6a) of the sun, and from the west, that there is none beside me. I am the Lord, and there is none else.

7 I form the [alight](#note7a), and create darkness: I make peace, and create [bevil](#note7b): I the Lord do all these things.

8 Drop down, ye heavens, from above, and let the skies pour down [arighteousness](#note8a): let the earth open, and let [bthem](#note8b) bring forth [csalvation](#note8c), and let righteousness spring up together; I the Lord have created it.

9 Woe unto him that [astriveth](#note9a) with his [bMaker](#note9b)! Let the potsherd strive with the potsherds of the earth. Shall the [cclay](#note9c) say to him that fashioneth it, What makest thou? or thy work, He hath no hands?

10 Woe unto him that saith unto his father, What begettest thou? or to [athe woman](#note10a), What hast thou brought forth?

11 Thus saith the Lord, the Holy One of Israel, and his Maker, Ask me of things to come concerning my [asons](#note11a), and concerning the [bwork](#note11b) of my hands [ccommand ye me](#note11c).

12 I have [amade](#note12a) the earth, and [bcreated](#note12b) man upon it: I, even my hands, have stretched out the heavens, and all their [chost](#note12c) have I commanded.

13 I have raised [ahim](#note13a) up in righteousness, and I will direct all his ways: he shall [bbuild](#note13b) my city, and he shall let go my captives, not for [cprice](#note13c) nor reward, saith the Lord of hosts.

14 Thus saith the Lord, The labour of [aEgypt](#note14a), and merchandise of Ethiopia and of the Sabeans, men of stature, shall come over unto thee, and they shall be thine: they shall come [bafter](#note14b) thee; in chains they shall come over, and they shall fall down unto thee, they shall make supplication unto thee, saying, Surely God is in thee; and there is [cnone](#note14c) else, there is no God.

15 Verily thou art a God that [ahidest](#note15a) thyself, O God of Israel, the [bSaviour](#note15b).

16 They shall be ashamed, and also confounded, all of them: they shall go to confusion together that are makers of [aidols](#note16a).

17 But Israel shall be [asaved](#note17a) in the [bLord](#note17b) with an everlasting [csalvation](#note17c): ye shall not be ashamed nor confounded world without end.

18 For thus saith the Lord that [acreated](#note18a) the heavens; God himself that formed the earth and made it; he hath established it, he created it not in vain, he formed it to be [binhabited](#note18b): I am the Lord; and there is none else.

19 I have not spoken in [asecret](#note19a), in a dark place of the earth: I said not unto the seed of Jacob, Seek ye me in vain: I the Lord speak [brighteousness](#note19b), I declare things that are [cright](#note19c).

20 ¶ Assemble yourselves and come; draw near together, ye that are [aescaped](#note20a) of the [bnations](#note20b): they have no [cknowledge](#note20c) that set up the wood of their graven image, and [dpray](#note20d) unto a god that cannot save.

21 Tell ye, and bring them near; yea, let them take counsel together: who hath declared this from ancient time? who hath told it from that time? have not I the Lord? and there is no God else beside me; a [ajust](#note21a) God and a [bSaviour](#note21b); there is none beside me.

22 [aLook](#note22a) unto me, and be ye [bsaved](#note22b), all the ends of the earth: for I am God, and there is none else.

23 I have sworn by myself, the word is gone out of my mouth in righteousness, and shall not return, That unto me every [aknee](#note23a) shall bow, every tongue shall [bswear](#note23b).

24 Surely, shall one say, in the Lord have I righteousness and [astrength](#note24a): even to him shall men come; and all that are incensed against him shall be ashamed.

25 In the Lord shall all the seed of Israel be [ajustified](#note25a), and shall glory.

Chapter 46

Idols are not to be compared with the Lord—He alone is God and will save Israel.

1 [aBel](#note1a) boweth down, Nebo stoopeth, their idols were upon the beasts, and upon the cattle: your carriages were heavy loaden; they are a [bburden](#note1b) to the weary beast.

2 [aThey](#note2a) stoop, they bow down together; they could not deliver the burden, but themselves are gone into captivity.

3 ¶ Hearken unto me, O house of Jacob, and all the [aremnant](#note3a) of the house of Israel, which are borne by me from the belly, which are carried from the womb:

4 And even to your [aold](#note4a) age I am he; and even to [bhoar hairs](#note4b) will I carry you: I have made, and I will bear; even I will [ccarry](#note4c), and will [ddeliver](#note4d) you.

5 ¶ To whom will ye [aliken](#note5a) me, and make me equal, and compare me, that we may be like?

6 They lavish gold out of the bag, and weigh silver in the balance, and hire a goldsmith; and he maketh it a god: they fall down, yea, they [aworship](#note6a).

7 They [abear](#note7a) him upon the shoulder, they carry him, and set him in his place, and he standeth; from his place shall he not remove: yea, one shall [bcry](#note7b) unto him, yet can he not answer, nor save him out of his trouble.

8 Remember this, and shew yourselves [amen](#note8a): bring it again to mind, O ye transgressors.

9 [aRemember](#note9a) the [bformer](#note9b) things of old: for [cI am](#note9c) God, and there is none else; I am God, and there is [dnone](#note9d) like me,

10 [aDeclaring](#note10a) the [bend](#note10b) from the beginning, and from ancient times the things that are not yet done, saying, My [ccounsel](#note10c) shall stand, and I will do all my [dpleasure](#note10d):

11 Calling a [aravenous bird](#note11a) from the [beast](#note11b), the man that executeth my counsel from a far country: yea, I have [cspoken](#note11c) it, I will also bring it to pass; I have purposed it, I will also do it.

12 ¶ Hearken unto me, ye [astouthearted](#note12a), that are far from righteousness:

13 I bring near my righteousness; it shall not be far off, and my [asalvation](#note13a) shall not [btarry](#note13b): and I will place salvation in Zion for Israel my glory.

Chapter 47

Babylon and Chaldea will be destroyed for their iniquities—No one will save them.

1 Come down, and sit in the dust, O virgin daughter of [aBabylon](#note1a), sit on the ground: there is no [bthrone](#note1b), O [cdaughter of the Chaldeans](#note1c): for thou shalt no more be called tender and delicate.

2 [aTake](#note2a) the millstones, and grind meal: uncover thy locks, make bare the leg, uncover the thigh, [bpass over the rivers](#note2b).

3 Thy nakedness shall be uncovered, yea, thy shame shall be seen: I will take vengeance, and [aI](#note3a) will not meet thee as a man.

4 As for our redeemer, the Lord of hosts is his name, the Holy One of Israel.

5 Sit thou silent, and [aget thee into darkness](#note5a), O daughter of the Chaldeans: for thou shalt no more be called, The lady of kingdoms.

6 ¶ I was wroth with my people, I have polluted mine inheritance, and [agiven](#note6a) them into thine hand: thou didst shew them no mercy; upon the ancient hast thou very heavily laid thy yoke.

7 ¶ And thou saidst, I shall be [aa lady](#note7a) for ever: so that thou didst not lay these things to thy heart, neither didst remember the latter [bend](#note7b) of it.

8 Therefore hear now this, thou that art given to pleasures, that dwellest carelessly, that sayest in thine heart, I am, and none else beside me; I shall not sit as a [awidow](#note8a), neither shall I know the [bloss of children](#note8b):

9 But these two things shall come to thee in a moment in one day, the loss of children, and widowhood: they shall come upon thee [ain their perfection](#note9a) for the multitude of thy sorceries, and for the great abundance of thine enchantments.

10 ¶ For thou hast trusted in thy wickedness: thou hast said, None [aseeth](#note10a) me. Thy wisdom and thy knowledge, it hath perverted thee; and thou hast said in thine heart, I am, and none else beside me.

11 ¶ Therefore shall evil come upon thee; thou shalt not know from whence it riseth: and [amischief](#note11a) shall fall upon thee; thou shalt not be able to put it off: and [bdesolation](#note11b) shall come upon thee suddenly, which thou shalt not know.

12 Stand now with thine enchantments, and with the multitude of thy sorceries, wherein thou hast laboured from thy youth; if so be thou shalt be able to profit, if so be thou mayest prevail.

13 Thou art wearied in the multitude of thy counsels. Let now the [aastrologers](#note13a), the stargazers, the [bmonthly](#note13b) prognosticators, stand up, and save thee from these things that shall come upon thee.

14 Behold, they shall be as [astubble](#note14a); the fire shall burn them; they shall not deliver themselves from the power of the flame: there shall not be a coal to warm at, nor fire to sit before it.

15 Thus shall they be unto thee with whom thou hast laboured, even thy merchants, from thy youth: they shall wander every one to his quarter; none shall save thee.

Chapter 48

The Lord reveals His purposes to Israel—Israel has been chosen in the furnace of affliction and is to depart from Babylon—Compare 1 Nephi 20.

1 Hear ye this, O house of Jacob, which are called by the name of Israel, and are come forth out of the [awaters of Judah](#note1a), which [bswear](#note1b) by the name of the Lord, and make [cmention](#note1c) of the God of Israel, but not in truth, nor in righteousness.

2 For they call themselves of the [aholy city](#note2a), and [bstay themselves upon](#note2b) the God of Israel; The Lord of hosts is his name.

3 I have [adeclared](#note3a) the [bformer](#note3b) things from the beginning; and they went forth out of my mouth, and I shewed them; I did them suddenly, and they came to pass.

4 Because I knew that [athou](#note4a) art [bobstinate](#note4b), and thy [cneck](#note4c) is an iron sinew, and thy brow brass;

5 I have even from the beginning declared it to thee; before it came to pass I shewed it thee: lest thou shouldest say, Mine idol hath done them, and my graven image, and my molten image, hath commanded them.

6 Thou hast heard, see all this; and will not ye declare it? I have shewed thee new things from this time, even hidden things, and thou didst not know them.

7 They are created now, and not from the beginning; even before the day when thou heardest them not; lest thou shouldest say, Behold, I knew them.

8 Yea, thou heardest not; yea, thou knewest not; yea, from that time that thine ear was not opened: for I knew that thou wouldest deal very treacherously, and wast called a transgressor from the [awomb](#note8a).

9 ¶ For my [aname’s](#note9a) sake will I defer mine [banger](#note9b), and for my praise will I refrain for thee, that I cut thee not off.

10 Behold, I have refined thee, but not with silver; I have chosen thee in the [afurnace](#note10a) of [baffliction](#note10b).

11 For mine own [asake](#note11a), even for mine own sake, will I do it: for how should my [bname](#note11b) be polluted? and I will not [cgive](#note11c) my glory unto another.

12 ¶ Hearken unto me, O Jacob and Israel, my called; I am he; I am the first, I also am the last.

13 Mine hand also hath laid the foundation of the [aearth](#note13a), and my right hand hath spanned the heavens: when I call unto them, they stand up together.

14 All ye, assemble yourselves, and hear; which among them hath declared these things? The Lord hath loved him: he will do his [apleasure](#note14a) on [bBabylon](#note14b), and his arm shall be on the Chaldeans.

15 I, even I, have spoken; yea, I have called him: I have brought him, and he shall make his way prosperous.

16 ¶ Come ye near unto me, hear ye this; I have not spoken in [asecret](#note16a) from the beginning; from the time that it was, there am I: and now the Lord God, and his Spirit, hath [bsent](#note16b) me.

17 Thus saith the Lord, thy Redeemer, the Holy One of Israel; I am the Lord thy God which teacheth thee to profit, which [aleadeth](#note17a) thee by the way that thou shouldest go.

18 O that thou hadst hearkened to my commandments! then had thy [apeace](#note18a) been as a river, and thy righteousness as the waves of the sea:

19 Thy [aseed](#note19a) also had been as the sand, and the offspring of thy bowels like the gravel thereof; his name should not have been cut off nor destroyed from before me.

20 ¶ Go ye forth of [aBabylon](#note20a), flee ye from the [bChaldeans](#note20b), with a voice of singing declare ye, tell this, utter it even to the end of the earth; say ye, The Lord hath redeemed his servant Jacob.

21 And they thirsted not when he led them through the deserts: he caused the [awaters](#note21a) to flow out of the rock for them: he clave the rock also, and the waters gushed out.

22 There is no [apeace](#note22a), saith the Lord, unto the wicked.

Chapter 49

The Messiah will be a light to the Gentiles and will free the prisoners—Israel will be gathered with power in the last days—Kings will be the nursing fathers of Israel—Compare 1 Nephi 21.

1 [aListen](#note1a), O isles, unto me; and [bhearken](#note1b), ye people, from far; The Lord hath [ccalled](#note1c) me from the womb; from the bowels of my mother hath he made mention of my name.

2 And he hath made my mouth like a sharp [asword](#note2a); in the shadow of his hand hath he hid me, and made me a polished shaft; in his quiver hath he hid me;

3 And said unto me, Thou art my [aservant](#note3a), O Israel, in whom I will be [bglorified](#note3b).

4 Then I said, I have laboured in vain, I have spent my strength for nought, and in vain: yet surely my judgment is with the Lord, and my work with my God.

5 ¶ And now, saith the Lord that [aformed](#note5a) me from the womb to be his servant, to bring Jacob again to him, Though Israel be not gathered, yet shall I be glorious in the eyes of the Lord, and my God shall be my strength.

6 And he said, It is a light thing that thou shouldest be my servant to raise up the tribes of Jacob, and to restore the preserved of Israel: I will also give thee for a [alight](#note6a) to the [bGentiles](#note6b), that thou mayest be my [csalvation](#note6c) unto the end of the earth.

7 Thus saith the Lord, the Redeemer of Israel, and his Holy One, to him whom man despiseth, to him whom the nation abhorreth, to a servant of rulers, Kings shall see and arise, princes also shall worship, because of the Lord that is faithful, and the Holy One of Israel, and he shall choose thee.

8 Thus saith the Lord, In an acceptable [atime](#note8a) have I heard thee, and in a day of salvation have I helped thee: and I will preserve thee, and give thee for a [bcovenant](#note8b) of the people, to establish the earth, to cause to [cinherit](#note8c) the desolate heritages;

9 That thou mayest say to the [aprisoners](#note9a), Go forth; to them that are in darkness, Shew yourselves. They shall feed in the ways, and their pastures shall be in all high places.

10 They shall not hunger nor [athirst](#note10a); neither shall the heat nor [bsun](#note10b) smite them: for he that hath mercy on them shall lead them, even by the springs of water shall he guide them.

11 And I will make all my mountains a way, and my [ahighways](#note11a) shall be exalted.

12 Behold, these shall come from far: and, lo, these from the [anorth](#note12a) and from the west; and these from the land of Sinim.

13 ¶ [aSing](#note13a), O heavens; and be joyful, O earth; and break forth into [bsinging](#note13b), O mountains: for the Lord hath [ccomforted](#note13c) his people, and will have [dmercy](#note13d) upon his [eafflicted](#note13e).

14 But Zion said, The Lord hath [aforsaken](#note14a) me, and my Lord hath forgotten me.

15 Can a [awoman](#note15a) forget her sucking child, that she should not have compassion on the son of her womb? yea, they may forget, yet will I not [bforget](#note15b) thee.

16 Behold, I have graven thee upon the palms of my hands; thy walls are continually before me.

17 Thy children shall make haste; thy destroyers and they that made thee waste shall go forth of thee.

18 ¶ Lift up thine eyes round about, and behold: all these [agather](#note18a) themselves together, and come to thee. As I live, saith the Lord, thou shalt surely clothe thee with them all, as with an ornament, and bind them on thee, as a bride doeth.

19 For thy waste and thy desolate places, and the land of thy destruction, shall even now be too narrow by reason of the inhabitants, and they that swallowed thee up shall be far away.

20 The children which thou shalt have, after thou hast lost the other, shall say again in thine ears, The place is too [astrait](#note20a) for me: give place to me that I may dwell.

21 Then shalt [athou](#note21a) say in thine heart, Who hath begotten me these, seeing I have lost my children, and am [bdesolate](#note21b), a captive, and removing to and fro? and who hath brought up these? Behold, I was left alone; these, where had they been?

22 Thus saith the Lord God, Behold, I will [alift up](#note22a) mine hand to the [bGentiles](#note22b), and set up my [cstandard](#note22c) to the people: and they shall bring thy [dsons](#note22d) in their arms, and thy daughters shall be carried upon their shoulders.

23 And kings shall be thy [anursing fathers](#note23a), and their queens thy nursing [bmothers](#note23b): they shall [cbow](#note23c) down to thee with their face toward the earth, and lick up the dust of thy feet; and thou shalt know that I am the Lord: for they shall not be [dashamed](#note23d) that wait for me.

24 ¶ Shall the prey be taken from the mighty, or the lawful captive delivered?

25 But thus saith the Lord, Even the captives of the mighty shall be taken away, and the prey of the terrible shall be delivered: for I will [acontend](#note25a) with him that contendeth with thee, and I will save thy children.

26 And I will feed them that [aoppress](#note26a) thee with their own flesh; and they shall be drunken with their own blood, as with sweet wine: and all flesh shall [bknow](#note26b) that I the Lord am thy [cSaviour](#note26c) and thy [dRedeemer](#note26d), the [emighty One](#note26e) of Jacob.

Chapter 50

Isaiah speaks as the Messiah—He will have the tongue of the learned—He will give His back to the smiters—He will not be confounded—Compare 2 Nephi 7.

1 [aThus](#note1a) saith the Lord, Where is the bill of your mother’s [bdivorcement](#note1b), whom I have put away? or which of my creditors is it to whom I have sold you? Behold, for your [ciniquities](#note1c) have ye sold yourselves, and for your transgressions is your [dmother](#note1d) put away.

2 Wherefore, when I came, was there no man? when I called, was there none to answer? Is my [ahand](#note2a) shortened at all, that it cannot redeem? or have I no [bpower](#note2b) to deliver? behold, at my rebuke I [cdry up](#note2c) the sea, I make the rivers a wilderness: their fish stinketh, because there is no water, and dieth for thirst.

3 I clothe the heavens with blackness, and I make sackcloth their covering.

4 The Lord God hath given me the tongue of the [alearned](#note4a), that I should know how to speak a [bword](#note4b) in season to him that is weary: he wakeneth morning by morning, he wakeneth mine ear to hear as the learned.

5 ¶ The Lord God hath opened mine [aear](#note5a), and I was not [brebellious](#note5b), neither turned away back.

6 I [agave](#note6a) my [bback](#note6b) to the [csmiters](#note6c), and my [dcheeks](#note6d) to them that plucked off the hair: I [ehid](#note6e) not my face from [fshame](#note6f) and [gspitting](#note6g).

7 ¶ For the Lord God will help me; therefore shall I not be confounded: therefore have I set my face like a flint, and I know that I shall not be ashamed.

8 He is near that [ajustifieth](#note8a) me; who will contend with me? let us stand together: who is mine adversary? let him come near to me.

9 Behold, the Lord God will help me; who is he that shall condemn me? lo, they all shall wax [aold](#note9a) as a garment; the [bmoth](#note9b) shall eat them up.

10 ¶ Who is among you that feareth the Lord, that obeyeth the [avoice](#note10a) of his [bservant](#note10b), that walketh in [cdarkness](#note10c), and hath no [dlight](#note10d)? let him [etrust](#note10e) in the name of the Lord, and [fstay upon](#note10f) his God.

11 Behold, all ye that kindle a fire, that compass yourselves about with sparks: walk in the [alight](#note11a) of your fire, and in the sparks that ye have kindled. This shall ye have of mine hand; ye shall lie down in [bsorrow](#note11b).

Chapter 51

In the last days, the Lord will comfort Zion and gather Israel—The redeemed will come to Zion amid great joy—Compare 2 Nephi 8.

1 [aHearken](#note1a) to me, ye that follow after righteousness, ye that seek the Lord: look unto the [brock](#note1b) whence ye are hewn, and to the hole of the pit whence ye are digged.

2 Look unto [aAbraham](#note2a) your [bfather](#note2b), and unto Sarah that bare you: for I called him [calone](#note2c), and [dblessed](#note2d) him, and increased him.

3 For the Lord shall [acomfort](#note3a) [bZion](#note3b): he will comfort all her waste places; and he will make her wilderness like [cEden](#note3c), and her desert like the [dgarden](#note3d) of the Lord; joy and gladness shall be found therein, thanksgiving, and the voice of melody.

4 ¶ Hearken unto me, my people; and give ear unto me, O my nation: for a [alaw](#note4a) shall proceed from me, and I will make my judgment to rest for a light of the people.

5 My righteousness is near; my [asalvation](#note5a) is gone forth, and mine arms shall [bjudge](#note5b) the people; the [cisles](#note5c) shall wait upon me, and on mine arm shall they trust.

6 Lift up your eyes to the heavens, and look upon the earth beneath: for the heavens shall [avanish away](#note6a) like smoke, and the earth shall [bwax](#note6b) [cold](#note6c) like a garment, and they that dwell therein shall die in like manner: but my salvation shall be for ever, and my righteousness shall not be abolished.

7 ¶ Hearken unto me, ye that know righteousness, the people in whose [aheart](#note7a) is my law; [bfear](#note7b) ye not the [creproach](#note7c) of [dmen](#note7d), neither be ye afraid of their [erevilings](#note7e).

8 For the [amoth](#note8a) shall eat them up like a garment, and the worm shall eat them like wool: but my righteousness shall be for ever, and my salvation from generation to generation.

9 ¶ Awake, awake, put on [astrength](#note9a), O arm of the Lord; awake, as in the ancient days, in the generations of old. Art thou not it that hath cut Rahab, and wounded the [bdragon](#note9b)?

10 Art thou not it which hath [adried](#note10a) the sea, the waters of the great deep; that hath made the depths of the sea a [bway](#note10b) for the [cransomed](#note10c) to pass over?

11 Therefore the [aredeemed](#note11a) of the Lord shall [breturn](#note11b), and come with singing unto Zion; and everlasting [cjoy](#note11c) shall be upon their head: they shall obtain gladness and joy; and sorrow and [dmourning](#note11d) shall flee away.

12 I, even I, am he that comforteth you: who art thou, that thou shouldest be [aafraid](#note12a) of a man that shall die, and of the son of man which shall be made as grass;

13 And [aforgettest](#note13a) the Lord thy maker, that hath stretched forth the heavens, and laid the foundations of the [bearth](#note13b); and hast feared continually every day because of the fury of the oppressor, as if he were ready to destroy? and where is the fury of the oppressor?

14 The captive exile hasteneth that he may be loosed, and that he should not die in the [apit](#note14a), nor that his bread should fail.

15 But I am the Lord thy God, that divided the [asea](#note15a), whose waves roared: The Lord of hosts is his name.

16 And I have put my [awords](#note16a) in thy mouth, and I have covered thee in the shadow of mine hand, that I may plant the heavens, and lay the foundations of the earth, and say unto Zion, Thou art my people.

17 ¶ Awake, awake, stand up, O Jerusalem, which hast drunk at the hand of the Lord the [acup](#note17a) of his [bfury](#note17b); thou hast drunken the dregs of the [ccup](#note17c) of trembling, and wrung them out.

18 There is none to guide her among all the sons whom she hath brought forth; neither is there any that taketh her by the hand of all the sons that she hath brought up.

19 These [atwo](#note19a) things are come unto thee; who shall be sorry for thee? desolation, and destruction, and the famine, and the sword: by whom shall I comfort thee?

20 Thy sons have fainted, they lie at the head of all the streets, as a [awild bull](#note20a) in a net: they are full of the fury of the Lord, the rebuke of thy God.

21 ¶ Therefore hear now this, thou afflicted, and drunken, but not with wine:

22 Thus saith thy Lord the Lord, and thy God that [apleadeth](#note22a) the cause of his people, Behold, I have taken out of thine hand the cup of trembling, even the dregs of the cup of my fury; thou shalt no more drink it again:

23 But I will put it into the [ahand](#note23a) of them that [bafflict](#note23b) thee; which have said to thy soul, [cBow down](#note23c), that we may go over: and thou hast laid thy body as the ground, and as the street, to them that went over.

Chapter 52

In the last days, Zion will return, and Israel will be redeemed—The Messiah will deal prudently and be exalted.

1 [aAwake](#note1a), awake; put on thy [bstrength](#note1b), O [cZion](#note1c); put on thy [dbeautiful](#note1d) [egarments](#note1e), O [fJerusalem](#note1f), the holy city: for henceforth there shall no more come into thee the uncircumcised and the unclean.

2 [aShake](#note2a) thyself from the dust; [barise, and sit down](#note2b), O Jerusalem: loose thyself from the [cbands](#note2c) of thy neck, O captive daughter of Zion.

3 For thus saith the Lord, Ye have [asold](#note3a) yourselves for nought; and ye shall be redeemed without [bmoney](#note3b).

4 For thus saith the Lord [aGod](#note4a), My people went down aforetime into [bEgypt](#note4b) to sojourn there; and the Assyrian oppressed them without cause.

5 Now therefore, what have I here, saith the Lord, that my people is taken away for nought? they that rule over them make them to howl, saith the Lord; and my name continually every day is [ablasphemed](#note5a).

6 Therefore my people shall know my name: therefore they shall know in that [aday](#note6a) that I am he that doth speak: behold, it is I.

7 ¶ How [abeautiful](#note7a) upon the mountains are the feet of him that [bbringeth](#note7b) [cgood](#note7c) [dtidings](#note7d), that [epublisheth](#note7e) [fpeace](#note7f); that bringeth good tidings of good, that publisheth salvation; that saith unto [gZion](#note7g), Thy God reigneth!

8 Thy [awatchmen](#note8a) shall lift up the voice; with the voice together shall they sing: for they shall [bsee](#note8b) eye to eye, when the Lord [cshall bring again](#note8c) [dZion](#note8d).

9 ¶ Break forth into joy, sing together, ye [awaste places](#note9a) of Jerusalem: for the Lord hath comforted his people, he hath redeemed Jerusalem.

10 The Lord hath made [abare](#note10a) his holy [barm](#note10b) in the eyes of all the nations; and all the ends of the earth shall [csee](#note10c) the [dsalvation](#note10d) of our God.

11 ¶ Depart ye, depart ye, go ye [aout](#note11a) from thence, [btouch](#note11b) no [cunclean thing](#note11c); go ye [dout](#note11d) of the midst of her; be ye [eclean](#note11e), that bear the vessels of the Lord.

12 For ye shall not go out with [ahaste](#note12a), nor go by flight: for the Lord will go before you; and the God of Israel will be your [brearward](#note12b).

13 ¶ Behold, my [aservant](#note13a) shall deal [bprudently](#note13b), he shall be exalted and extolled, and be very high.

14 As many were [aastonied](#note14a) at thee; his [bvisage](#note14b) was so marred more than any man, and his form more than the sons of men:

15 So shall he [asprinkle](#note15a) many nations; the kings shall shut their mouths at him: for that which had not been [btold](#note15b) them shall they see; and that which they had not heard shall they consider.

Chapter 53

Isaiah speaks about the Messiah—His humiliation and sufferings are described—He makes His soul an offering for sin and makes intercession for the transgressors—Compare Mosiah 14.

1 Who hath [abelieved](#note1a) our report? and to whom is the arm of the Lord revealed?

2 For he shall grow up before him as a tender [aplant](#note2a), and as a [broot](#note2b) out of a [cdry](#note2c) ground: he hath no form nor comeliness; and when we shall see him, there is no [dbeauty](#note2d) that we should desire him.

3 He is [adespised](#note3a) and rejected of men; a man of [bsorrows](#note3b), and acquainted with grief: and we hid as it were our faces from him; he was despised, and we [cesteemed](#note3c) him not.

4 ¶ Surely he hath [aborne](#note4a) our [bgriefs](#note4b), and carried our sorrows: yet we did esteem him stricken, smitten of God, and afflicted.

5 But he was [awounded](#note5a) for our [btransgressions](#note5b), he was bruised for our iniquities: the chastisement of our peace was upon him; and with his [cstripes](#note5c) we are [dhealed](#note5d).

6 All we like [asheep](#note6a) have gone [bastray](#note6b); we have turned every one to his [cown](#note6c) way; and the Lord hath laid on him the [diniquity](#note6d) of us all.

7 He was [aoppressed](#note7a), and he was [bafflicted](#note7b), yet he [copened](#note7c) not his mouth: he is brought as a [dlamb](#note7d) to the [eslaughter](#note7e), and as a sheep before her shearers is dumb, so he openeth not his mouth.

8 He was taken from prison and from judgment: and who shall declare his [ageneration](#note8a)? for he was cut off out of the land of the living: for the [btransgression](#note8b) of my people was he stricken.

9 And he made his grave with the [awicked](#note9a), and with the rich in his [bdeath](#note9b); [cbecause](#note9c) he had done no [dviolence](#note9d), neither was any [edeceit](#note9e) in his mouth.

10 ¶ Yet it pleased the Lord to [abruise](#note10a) him; he hath put him to grief: when thou shalt make his soul an [boffering](#note10b) for sin, he shall see his [cseed](#note10c), he shall prolong his days, and the [dpleasure](#note10d) of the Lord shall prosper in his hand.

11 He shall see of the travail of his soul, and shall be satisfied: by his [aknowledge](#note11a) shall my righteous [bservant](#note11b) [cjustify](#note11c) many; for he shall [dbear](#note11d) their iniquities.

12 Therefore will I divide him a portion with the great, and he shall divide the spoil with the strong; because he hath poured out his soul unto [adeath](#note12a): and he was numbered with the [btransgressors](#note12b); and he bare the sin of many, and made [cintercession](#note12c) for the transgressors.

Chapter 54

In the last days, Zion and her stakes will be established, and Israel will be gathered in mercy and tenderness—Israel will triumph—Compare 3 Nephi 22.

1 [aSing](#note1a), O [bbarren](#note1b), thou that didst not bear; break forth into singing, and cry aloud, thou that didst not travail with child: for more are the children of the desolate than the children of the married wife, saith the Lord.

2 Enlarge the place of thy tent, and let them stretch forth the curtains of thine habitations: spare not, lengthen thy cords, and strengthen thy [astakes](#note2a);

3 For thou shalt break forth on the right hand and on the left; and thy seed shall inherit the Gentiles, and make the desolate cities to be inhabited.

4 Fear not; for thou shalt not be ashamed: neither be thou confounded; for thou shalt not be put to shame: for thou shalt forget the [ashame](#note4a) of thy youth, and shalt not remember the [breproach](#note4b) of thy widowhood any more.

5 For thy Maker is thine [ahusband](#note5a); the [bLord of hosts](#note5b) is his name; and thy [cRedeemer](#note5c) the Holy One of Israel; The [dGod](#note5d) of the whole earth shall he be called.

6 For the Lord hath called thee as a [awoman](#note6a) [bforsaken](#note6b) and grieved in spirit, and a [cwife](#note6c) of youth, [dwhen thou wast refused](#note6d), saith thy God.

7 For a small [amoment](#note7a) have I [bforsaken](#note7b) thee; but with great mercies will I [cgather](#note7c) thee.

8 In a little [awrath](#note8a) I [bhid](#note8b) my [cface](#note8c) from thee for a moment; but with everlasting [dkindness](#note8d) will I have [emercy](#note8e) on thee, saith the Lord thy Redeemer.

9 For this is as the waters of Noah unto me: for as I have sworn that the [awaters of Noah](#note9a) should no more go over the earth; so have I sworn that I would not be wroth with thee, nor rebuke thee.

10 For the [amountains](#note10a) shall depart, and the hills be removed; but my kindness shall not depart from thee, neither shall the [bcovenant](#note10b) of my peace be removed, saith the Lord that hath mercy on thee.

11 ¶ O thou afflicted, tossed with tempest, and not comforted, behold, I will lay thy [astones](#note11a) with fair colours, and lay thy foundations with sapphires.

12 And I will make thy windows of agates, and thy gates of carbuncles, and all thy borders of pleasant stones.

13 And all thy [achildren](#note13a) shall be [btaught](#note13b) of the Lord; and great shall be the [cpeace](#note13c) of thy children.

14 In righteousness shalt thou be established: thou shalt be far from oppression; for thou shalt not fear: and from terror; for it shall not come near thee.

15 Behold, they shall surely gather together, but not by me: whosoever shall gather together against thee shall fall for thy sake.

16 Behold, I have created the smith that bloweth the coals in the fire, and that bringeth forth an instrument for his work; and I have created the [awaster](#note16a) to destroy.

17 ¶ No [aweapon](#note17a) that is formed against thee shall prosper; and every [btongue](#note17b) that shall rise against thee in judgment thou shalt condemn. This is the heritage of the [cservants](#note17c) of the Lord, and their righteousness is of me, saith the Lord.

  c

  TG Servant.

Chapter 55

Come and drink; salvation is free—The Lord will make an everlasting covenant with Israel—Seek the Lord while He is near.

1 Ho, every one that [athirsteth](#note1a), come ye to the [bwaters](#note1b), and he that hath no money; come ye, buy, and eat; yea, come, [cbuy](#note1c) wine and milk without money and without [dprice](#note1d).

2 Wherefore do ye [aspend](#note2a) money for that which is not bread? and your [blabour](#note2b) for that which satisfieth not? hearken [cdiligently](#note2c) unto me, and eat ye that which is good, and let your soul delight itself in fatness.

3 Incline your ear, and [acome](#note3a) unto me: hear, and your [bsoul](#note3b) shall live; and I will make an everlasting [ccovenant](#note3c) with you, even the [dsure](#note3d) mercies of David.

4 Behold, I have given him for a [awitness](#note4a) to the people, a [bleader](#note4b) and commander to the people.

5 Behold, thou shalt call a nation that thou knowest not, and [anations](#note5a) that knew not thee shall run unto thee because of the Lord thy God, and for the Holy One of Israel; for he hath glorified thee.

6 ¶ [aSeek](#note6a) ye the [bLord](#note6b) while he may be found, call ye upon him while he is near:

7 Let the wicked forsake his way, and the unrighteous man his thoughts: and let him [areturn](#note7a) unto the Lord, and he will have mercy upon him; and to our God, for he will abundantly [bpardon](#note7b).

8 ¶ For my [athoughts](#note8a) are not [byour](#note8b) thoughts, neither are your [cways](#note8c) my [dways](#note8d), saith the Lord.

9 For as the heavens are higher than the earth, so are my [aways](#note9a) [bhigher](#note9b) than your ways, and my [cthoughts](#note9c) than your thoughts.

10 For as the [arain](#note10a) cometh down, and the snow from heaven, and returneth not thither, but watereth the earth, and maketh it bring forth and bud, that it may give seed to the sower, and [bbread](#note10b) to the eater:

11 So shall my [aword](#note11a) be that goeth forth out of my mouth: it shall not return unto me void, but it shall accomplish that which I please, and it shall prosper in the thing whereto I sent it.

12 For ye shall go out with [ajoy](#note12a), and be led forth with peace: the mountains and the hills shall break forth before you into singing, and all the [btrees](#note12b) of the field shall clap their hands.

13 Instead of the thorn shall come up the [afir tree](#note13a), and instead of the brier shall come up the myrtle tree: and it shall be to the Lord for a name, for an everlasting sign that shall not be cut off.

Chapter 56

All who keep the commandments will be exalted—Other people will join Israel—The Lord will gather others to the house of Israel.

1 Thus saith the Lord, Keep ye judgment, and do [ajustice](#note1a): for my salvation is [bnear](#note1b) to come, and my righteousness to be revealed.

2 Blessed is the man that doeth this, and the son of man that layeth hold on it; that keepeth the [asabbath](#note2a) from polluting it, and keepeth his hand from doing any [bevil](#note2b).

3 ¶ Neither let the [ason](#note3a) of the [bstranger](#note3b), that hath joined himself to the Lord, speak, saying, The Lord hath utterly separated me from his people: neither let the eunuch say, Behold, I am a dry tree.

4 For thus saith the Lord unto the eunuchs that keep my sabbaths, and choose the things that please me, and take hold of my covenant;

5 Even unto them will I give in mine [ahouse](#note5a) and within my walls a place and a name better than of [bsons](#note5b) and of daughters: I will give them an everlasting name, that shall not be cut off.

6 Also the sons of the stranger, that join themselves to the Lord, to serve him, and to love the name of the Lord, to be his servants, every one that keepeth the sabbath from polluting it, and taketh hold of my covenant;

7 Even them will I bring to my holy [amountain](#note7a), and make them joyful in my [bhouse](#note7b) of [cprayer](#note7c): their burnt offerings and their sacrifices shall be [daccepted](#note7d) upon mine altar; for mine [ehouse](#note7e) shall be called an house of prayer for [fall](#note7f) [gpeople](#note7g).

8 The Lord God which [agathereth](#note8a) the outcasts of Israel saith, Yet will I gather [bothers](#note8b) to him, beside those that are gathered unto him.

9 ¶ [aAll](#note9a) ye beasts of the field, come to devour, yea, all ye beasts in the forest.

10 His [awatchmen](#note10a) are [bblind](#note10b): they are all ignorant, they are all dumb dogs, they cannot bark; sleeping, lying down, loving to slumber.

11 Yea, they are [agreedy](#note11a) dogs which can never have enough, and they are [bshepherds](#note11b) that cannot understand: they all look to their [cown](#note11c) way, every one for his gain, from his quarter.

12 Come ye, say they, I will fetch wine, and we will fill ourselves with strong drink; and to morrow shall be as this day, and much more abundant.

Chapter 57

When the righteous die, they enter into peace—Mercy is promised to the penitent—There is no peace for the wicked.

1 The righteous [aperisheth](#note1a), and no man layeth it to heart: and merciful men are taken away, none considering that the righteous is taken away from the evil to come.

2 He shall enter into [apeace](#note2a): they shall rest in their beds, each one walking in his uprightness.

3 ¶ But draw near hither, ye [asons](#note3a) of the sorceress, the seed of the [badulterer](#note3b) and the whore.

4 Against whom do ye sport yourselves? against whom make ye a wide mouth, and draw out the tongue? are ye not [achildren](#note4a) of transgression, a seed of falsehood,

5 Enflaming yourselves with [aidols](#note5a) under every green tree, [bslaying](#note5b) the [cchildren](#note5c) in the valleys under the clifts of the rocks?

6 Among the smooth stones of the stream is thy portion; they, they are thy lot: even to them hast thou poured a drink offering, thou hast offered a meat offering. Should I receive comfort in these?

7 Upon a lofty and high mountain hast thou set thy [abed](#note7a): even thither wentest thou up to offer sacrifice.

8 Behind the doors also and the posts hast thou set up thy remembrance: for thou hast [adiscovered](#note8a) thyself to [banother](#note8b) than me, and art gone up; thou hast enlarged thy bed, and made thee a covenant with them; thou lovedst their bed where thou sawest it.

9 And thou wentest to the [aking](#note9a) with ointment, and didst increase thy perfumes, and didst send thy messengers far off, and didst debase thyself even unto hell.

10 Thou art wearied in the greatness of thy way; yet saidst thou not, There is no [ahope](#note10a): thou hast found the [blife of thine hand](#note10b); therefore thou wast not grieved.

11 And of whom hast thou been afraid or [afeared](#note11a), that thou hast [blied](#note11b), and hast not remembered me, nor laid it to thy heart? have not I held my peace even of old, and thou fearest me not?

12 I will [adeclare](#note12a) thy righteousness, and thy works; for they shall not profit thee.

13 ¶ When thou criest, let thy companies deliver thee; but the wind shall carry them all away; vanity shall take them: but he that putteth his trust in me shall possess the land, and shall inherit my holy [amountain](#note13a);

14 [aAnd shall say](#note14a), Cast ye up, cast ye up, [bprepare](#note14b) the way, take up the [cstumblingblock](#note14c) out of the way of my people.

15 For thus saith the high and lofty One that inhabiteth [aeternity](#note15a), whose name is [bHoly](#note15b); I dwell in the high and holy place, with him also that is of a [ccontrite](#note15c) and [dhumble](#note15d) spirit, to [erevive](#note15e) the spirit of the [fhumble](#note15f), and to revive the heart of the contrite ones.

16 For I will not [acontend](#note16a) for ever, neither will I be always wroth: for the spirit should fail before me, and the [bsouls](#note16b) which I have made.

17 For the [ainiquity](#note17a) of his [bcovetousness](#note17b) was I wroth, and smote him: I hid me, and was wroth, and he went on [cfrowardly](#note17c) in the way of his heart.

18 I have seen his ways, and will heal him: I will [alead](#note18a) him also, and restore [bcomforts](#note18b) unto him and to his [cmourners](#note18c).

19 I create the [afruit](#note19a) of the lips; Peace, peace to him that is [bfar](#note19b) off, and to him that is near, saith the Lord; and I will heal him.

20 But the [awicked](#note20a) are like the troubled sea, when it cannot rest, whose waters cast up mire and dirt.

21 There is no [apeace](#note21a), saith my God, to the wicked.

Chapter 58

The true law of the fast, with its purposes and attendant blessings, is set forth—The commandment to keep the Sabbath is given.

1 Cry aloud, [aspare](#note1a) not, lift up thy [bvoice](#note1b) like a [ctrumpet](#note1c), and [dshew](#note1d) my people their [etransgression](#note1e), and the house of Jacob their sins.

2 [aYet](#note2a) they seek me daily, and delight to know my ways, as a nation that did righteousness, and forsook not the ordinance of their God: they ask of me the [bordinances](#note2b) of justice; they take delight in approaching to God.

3 ¶ [aWherefore](#note3a) have we fasted, say they, and thou seest not? wherefore have we afflicted our soul, and thou takest no knowledge? Behold, in the day of your [bfast](#note3b) ye find [cpleasure](#note3c), and [dexact all your labours](#note3d).

4 Behold, ye fast for [astrife](#note4a) and [bdebate](#note4b), and to smite with the fist of wickedness: ye shall not [cfast](#note4c) as ye do this day, to make your voice to be heard on high.

5 Is it such a fast that I have chosen? a day for a man to afflict his soul? is it to bow down his head as a bulrush, and to spread sackcloth and ashes under him? wilt thou call this a fast, and an acceptable day to the Lord?

6 Is not this the fast that I have chosen? to loose the [abands](#note6a) of wickedness, to undo the heavy burdens, and to let the oppressed go [bfree](#note6b), and that ye break every yoke?

7 Is it not to deal thy bread to the [ahungry](#note7a), and that thou bring the [bpoor](#note7b) that are cast out to thy house? when thou seest the naked, that thou cover him; and that thou hide not thyself from [cthine own flesh](#note7c)?

8 ¶ Then shall thy [alight](#note8a) break forth as the morning, and thine [bhealth](#note8b) shall spring forth speedily: and thy righteousness shall go before thee; the glory of the Lord shall be thy [crearward](#note8c).

9 Then shalt thou [acall](#note9a), and the Lord shall answer; thou shalt cry, and he shall say, Here I am. If thou take away from the midst of thee the yoke, the [bputting](#note9b) forth of the finger, and speaking vanity;

10 And if thou draw out thy soul to the [ahungry](#note10a), and satisfy the afflicted soul; then shall thy light [brise in obscurity](#note10b), and thy darkness be as the noonday:

11 And the Lord shall [aguide](#note11a) thee continually, and satisfy thy soul in [bdrought](#note11b), and [cmake fat](#note11c) thy bones: and thou shalt be like a watered garden, and like a [dspring](#note11d) of water, whose waters fail not.

12 And they that shall be of thee shall build the old waste places: thou shalt raise up the foundations of many generations; and thou shalt be called, The repairer of the breach, The restorer of paths to dwell in.

13 ¶ If thou turn away thy foot from the sabbath, from doing thy pleasure on my holy day; and call the [asabbath](#note13a) a delight, the holy of the Lord, honourable; and shalt honour him, not doing thine own ways, nor finding thine own pleasure, nor speaking thine own words:

14 Then shalt thou delight thyself in the Lord; and I will cause thee to ride upon the [ahigh places](#note14a) of the earth, and feed thee with the heritage of Jacob thy father: for the mouth of the Lord hath spoken it.

Chapter 59

The people of Israel are separated from their God by iniquity—Their sins testify against them—The Messiah will intercede, come to Zion, and redeem the repentant.

1 Behold, the Lord’s [ahand](#note1a) is not [bshortened](#note1b), that it cannot save; neither his ear heavy, that it cannot [chear](#note1c):

2 But your iniquities have [aseparated](#note2a) between you and your God, and your [bsins](#note2b) [chave hid](#note2c) his face from you, that he will not [dhear](#note2d).

3 For your hands are defiled with [ablood](#note3a), and your fingers with iniquity; your lips have spoken lies, your tongue hath muttered perverseness.

4 None calleth for justice, nor any pleadeth for truth: they [atrust](#note4a) in vanity, and speak lies; they conceive [bmischief](#note4b), and bring forth iniquity.

5 They hatch cockatrice’ eggs, and weave the spider’s web: he that eateth of their eggs dieth, and that which is crushed breaketh out into a viper.

6 Their webs shall not become garments, neither shall they cover themselves with their works: their works are works of iniquity, and the act of violence is in their hands.

7 Their feet [arun](#note7a) to [bevil](#note7b), and they make [chaste](#note7c) to [dshed](#note7d) innocent blood: their thoughts are thoughts of iniquity; wasting and destruction are in their paths.

8 The way of [apeace](#note8a) they know not; and there is no [bjudgment](#note8b) in their goings: they have made them [ccrooked](#note8c) paths: whosoever goeth therein shall not know peace.

9 ¶ Therefore is judgment far from us, neither doth [ajustice](#note9a) overtake us: we wait for [blight](#note9b), but behold obscurity; for brightness, but we [cwalk](#note9c) in darkness.

10 We [agrope](#note10a) for the wall like the blind, and we grope as if we had no eyes: we stumble at noonday as in the night; we are in desolate places as dead men.

11 We roar all like bears, and mourn sore like doves: we look for judgment, but there is none; for salvation, but it is far off from us.

12 For our transgressions are multiplied before thee, and our sins [atestify](#note12a) against us: for our transgressions are with us; and as for our iniquities, we [bknow](#note12b) them;

13 In transgressing and lying against the Lord, and departing away from our God, speaking oppression and revolt, conceiving and uttering from the heart words of falsehood.

14 And judgment is turned away backward, and justice standeth afar off: for truth is fallen in the street, and [aequity](#note14a) cannot enter.

15 Yea, truth faileth; and he that departeth from evil maketh himself a prey: and the Lord saw it, and it displeased him that there was no judgment.

16 ¶ And he saw that there was [ano man](#note16a), and wondered that there was no [bintercessor](#note16b): therefore his [carm](#note16c) [dbrought](#note16d) [esalvation](#note16e) unto him; and his righteousness, it sustained him.

17 For he put on [arighteousness](#note17a) as a [bbreastplate](#note17b), and an helmet of salvation upon his head; and he put on the garments of vengeance for clothing, and was clad with zeal as a cloak.

18 According to their [adeeds](#note18a), accordingly he will [brepay](#note18b), fury to his adversaries, [crecompence](#note18c) to his enemies; to the islands he will repay recompence.

19 So shall they [afear](#note19a) the [bname](#note19b) of the Lord from the west, and his glory from the rising of the sun. When the enemy shall come in like a flood, the [cSpirit](#note19c) of the Lord shall lift up a standard against him.

20 ¶ And the [aRedeemer](#note20a) shall [bcome](#note20b) to [cZion](#note20c), and unto them that [dturn](#note20d) from transgression in Jacob, saith the Lord.

21 As for me, this is my [acovenant](#note21a) with them, saith the Lord; My spirit that is upon thee, and my words which I have put in thy mouth, shall not depart out of thy mouth, nor out of the mouth of thy seed, nor out of the mouth of thy seed’s seed, saith the Lord, from henceforth and for ever.

Chapter 60

In the last days, Israel will rise again as a mighty nation—The gentile peoples will join with and serve Israel—Zion will be established—Finally, Israel will dwell in celestial splendor.

1 [aArise](#note1a), shine; for thy [blight](#note1b) is come, and the glory of the Lord is risen upon thee.

2 For, behold, the [adarkness](#note2a) shall cover the earth, and gross [bdarkness](#note2b) the people: but the Lord shall [carise upon thee](#note2c), and his [dglory](#note2d) shall be seen upon thee.

3 And the [aGentiles](#note3a) shall come to thy [blight](#note3b), and kings to the brightness of thy rising.

4 Lift up thine eyes round about, and see: all they gather themselves together, they come to thee: thy [asons](#note4a) shall come from far, and thy daughters shall be nursed at thy side.

5 Then thou shalt see, and [aflow together](#note5a), and thine heart shall fear, and be enlarged; because the [babundance](#note5b) of the sea shall be converted unto thee, the [cforces](#note5c) of the [dGentiles](#note5d) shall come unto thee.

6 The multitude of camels shall cover thee, the dromedaries of Midian and Ephah; all they from Sheba shall come: they shall bring [agold](#note6a) and incense; and they shall shew forth the praises of the Lord.

7 All the flocks of [aKedar](#note7a) shall be gathered together unto thee, the rams of Nebaioth shall minister unto thee: they shall come up with [bacceptance](#note7b) on mine [caltar](#note7c), and I will glorify the house of my [dglory](#note7d).

8 Who are [athese](#note8a) that fly as a cloud, and as the doves to their windows?

9 Surely the [aisles](#note9a) shall wait for me, and the ships of Tarshish first, to [bbring](#note9b) thy sons from far, their silver and their gold with them, unto the name of the Lord thy God, and to the Holy One of Israel, because he hath glorified thee.

10 And the [asons](#note10a) of strangers shall [bbuild](#note10b) up thy walls, and their kings shall minister unto thee: for in my [cwrath](#note10c) I smote thee, but in my favour have I had mercy on thee.

11 Therefore thy [agates](#note11a) shall be open continually; they shall not be shut day nor night; that men may bring unto thee the [bforces of the Gentiles](#note11b), and that their kings may be brought.

12 For the [anation](#note12a) and [bkingdom](#note12b) that will not serve thee shall [cperish](#note12c); yea, those [dnations](#note12d) shall be utterly wasted.

13 The glory of [aLebanon](#note13a) shall come unto thee, the [bfir](#note13b) tree, the pine tree, and the box together, to [cbeautify](#note13c) the place of my sanctuary; and I will make the place of my [dfeet](#note13d) glorious.

14 The sons also of them that afflicted thee shall come bending unto thee; and all they that despised thee shall [abow](#note14a) themselves down at the soles of thy feet; and they shall call thee, The city of the Lord, The Zion of the Holy One of Israel.

15 Whereas thou hast been [aforsaken](#note15a) and hated, so that no man went through thee, I will make thee an eternal excellency, a joy of many generations.

16 Thou shalt also suck the [amilk](#note16a) of the Gentiles, and shalt suck the breast of [bkings](#note16b): and thou shalt know that I the Lord am thy [cSaviour](#note16c) and thy Redeemer, the mighty One of Jacob.

17 For brass I will bring gold, and for iron I will bring silver, and for wood brass, and for stones iron: I will also make thy officers peace, and thine exactors righteousness.

18 [aViolence](#note18a) shall no more be heard in thy land, wasting nor destruction within thy borders; but thou shalt call thy [bwalls](#note18b) Salvation, and thy gates [cPraise](#note18c).

19 The [asun](#note19a) shall be no more thy light by day; neither for brightness shall the moon give light unto thee: but the Lord shall be unto thee an everlasting [blight](#note19b), and thy God thy glory.

20 Thy sun shall no more go down; neither shall thy moon withdraw itself: for the Lord shall be thine [aeverlasting](#note20a) light, and the days of thy [bmourning](#note20b) shall be ended.

21 Thy people also shall be all [arighteous](#note21a): they shall inherit the [bland](#note21b) for [cever](#note21c), the [dbranch](#note21d) of my planting, the [ework](#note21e) of my hands, that I may be glorified.

22 A [alittle one](#note22a) shall become a thousand, and a small one a [bstrong](#note22b) nation: I the Lord will hasten it in [chis](#note22c) time.

Chapter 61

Isaiah speaks about the Messiah—The Messiah will have the Spirit, preach the gospel, and proclaim liberty—In the last days, the Lord will call His ministers and make an everlasting covenant with the people.

1 The [aSpirit](#note1a) of the Lord [bGod](#note1b) is upon me; because the Lord hath [canointed](#note1c) me to [dpreach](#note1d) [egood tidings](#note1e) unto the [fmeek](#note1f); he hath sent me to [gbind](#note1g) up the brokenhearted, to [hproclaim](#note1h) [iliberty](#note1i) to the [jcaptives](#note1j), and the opening of the [kprison](#note1k) to them that are bound;

2 To proclaim the acceptable year of the Lord, and the day of [avengeance](#note2a) of our God; to [bcomfort](#note2b) all that [cmourn](#note2c);

3 To appoint unto them that mourn in Zion, to give unto them [abeauty](#note3a) for ashes, the oil of [bjoy](#note3b) for mourning, the garment of praise for the spirit of heaviness; that they might be called [ctrees](#note3c) of [drighteousness](#note3d), the [eplanting](#note3e) of the Lord, that he might be glorified.

4 ¶ And they shall [abuild](#note4a) the old wastes, they shall raise up the former desolations, and they shall repair the waste cities, the desolations of many generations.

5 And strangers shall stand and feed your flocks, and the sons of the alien shall be your plowmen and your vinedressers.

6 But ye shall be named the [aPriests](#note6a) of the Lord: men shall call you the Ministers of our God: ye shall eat the [briches](#note6b) of the Gentiles, and in their glory shall ye boast yourselves.

7 ¶ For your shame ye shall have [adouble](#note7a); and for confusion they shall rejoice in their portion: therefore in their land they shall possess [bthe double](#note7b): everlasting joy shall be unto them.

8 For I the Lord love [ajudgment](#note8a), I hate robbery for burnt offering; and I will direct their work in truth, and I will make an everlasting [bcovenant](#note8b) with them.

9 And their seed shall be known among the Gentiles, and their offspring among the people: all that see them shall acknowledge them, that they are the [aseed](#note9a) which the Lord hath blessed.

10 I will greatly rejoice in the Lord, my soul shall be joyful in my God; for he hath [aclothed](#note10a) me with the [bgarments](#note10b) of salvation, he hath covered me with the robe of righteousness, as a bridegroom decketh himself with ornaments, and as a bride adorneth herself with her jewels.

11 For as the earth bringeth forth her bud, and as the garden causeth the things that are sown in it to spring forth; so the Lord God will cause righteousness and [apraise](#note11a) to spring forth before all the nations.

Chapter 62

In the last days, Israel will be gathered—Zion will be established—Her watchmen will teach about the Lord—The gospel standard will be lifted up—The people will be called holy, the redeemed of the Lord.

1 For Zion’s sake will I not hold my peace, and for Jerusalem’s sake I will not rest, until the righteousness thereof go forth as brightness, and the salvation thereof as a lamp that burneth.

2 And the Gentiles shall [asee](#note2a) thy righteousness, and all kings thy glory: and thou shalt be called by a new [bname](#note2b), which the mouth of the Lord shall name.

3 Thou shalt also be a [acrown](#note3a) of glory in the hand of the Lord, and a royal diadem in the hand of thy God.

4 Thou shalt no more be termed [aForsaken](#note4a); neither shall thy [bland](#note4b) any more be termed Desolate: but thou shalt be called [cHephzi-bah](#note4c), and thy land [dBeulah](#note4d): for the Lord delighteth in thee, and thy land shall be married.

5 ¶ For as a young man marrieth a virgin, so shall thy sons marry thee: and as the bridegroom rejoiceth over the bride, so shall thy God [arejoice](#note5a) over thee.

6 I have set [awatchmen](#note6a) upon thy walls, O Jerusalem, which shall never hold their peace day nor night: ye that make mention of the Lord, keep not silence,

7 And give him no rest, till he establish, and till he make Jerusalem a [apraise](#note7a) in the earth.

8 The Lord hath sworn by his right hand, and by the arm of his strength, Surely I will no more give thy corn to be meat for thine enemies; and the sons of the stranger shall not drink thy wine, for the which thou hast laboured:

9 But they that have gathered it shall eat it, and praise the Lord; and they that have brought it together shall drink it in the courts of my [aholiness](#note9a).

10 ¶ Go through, go through the gates; [aprepare](#note10a) ye the way of the people; cast up, cast up the [bhighway](#note10b); gather out the stones; lift up a [cstandard](#note10c) for the people.

11 Behold, the Lord hath proclaimed unto the end of the [aworld](#note11a), Say ye to the [bdaughter](#note11b) of Zion, Behold, thy [csalvation](#note11c) cometh; behold, his [dreward](#note11d) is with him, and his work before him.

12 And they shall call them, The holy people, The redeemed of the Lord: and thou shalt be called, Sought out, A city not forsaken.

Chapter 63

The Second Coming will be a day of vengeance and also the year of the redeemed of the Lord—Then the Saints will praise the Lord and acknowledge Him as their father.

1 Who is this that [acometh](#note1a) from [bEdom](#note1b), with dyed garments from Bozrah? this that is glorious in his apparel, travelling in the greatness of his strength? I that speak in righteousness, mighty to save.

2 Wherefore art thou [ared](#note2a) in thine apparel, and thy garments like him that treadeth in the [bwinefat](#note2b)?

3 I have trodden the [awinepress](#note3a) alone; and of the people there was none with me: for I will tread them in mine anger, and trample them in my fury; and their blood shall be [bsprinkled](#note3b) upon my garments, and I will stain all my raiment.

4 For the day of [avengeance](#note4a) is in mine heart, and the year of my [bredeemed](#note4b) is come.

5 And I looked, and there was none to help; and I wondered that there was none to uphold: therefore mine own arm brought [asalvation](#note5a) unto me; and my fury, it upheld me.

6 And I will tread down the people in mine anger, and [amake them drunk](#note6a) in my fury, and I will bring down their strength to the earth.

7 ¶ I will mention the [alovingkindnesses](#note7a) of the Lord, and the praises of the Lord, according to all that the Lord hath bestowed on us, and the great [bgoodness](#note7b) toward the house of Israel, which he hath bestowed on them according to his mercies, and according to the multitude of his lovingkindnesses.

8 For he said, Surely they are my people, children that will not lie: so he was their [aSaviour](#note8a).

9 In all their [aaffliction](#note9a) he was afflicted, and the [bangel](#note9b) of his [cpresence](#note9c) saved them: in his [dlove](#note9d) and in his pity he [eredeemed](#note9e) them; and he bare them, and [fcarried](#note9f) them all the days of old.

10 ¶ But they [arebelled](#note10a), and [bvexed](#note10b) his [choly Spirit](#note10c): therefore he was turned to be their [denemy](#note10d), and he fought against them.

11 Then [ahe remembered](#note11a) the days of old, Moses, and his people, saying, Where is he that brought them up out of the [bsea](#note11b) with the [cshepherd](#note11c) of his [dflock](#note11d)? where is he that put his holy Spirit within [ehim](#note11e)?

12 That led them by the right hand of [aMoses](#note12a) with his glorious arm, [bdividing](#note12b) the water before them, to make himself an everlasting name?

13 That led them through the deep, as an horse in the wilderness, that they should not stumble?

14 [aAs a beast goeth](#note14a) down into the valley, the [bSpirit](#note14b) of the Lord caused [chim](#note14c) to rest: so didst thou lead thy people, to make thyself a glorious [dname](#note14d).

15 ¶ [aLook](#note15a) down from heaven, and behold from the habitation of thy [bholiness](#note15b) and of thy glory: where is thy zeal and thy strength, [cthe](#note15c) sounding of thy bowels and of thy mercies toward me? are they restrained?

16 Doubtless thou art our [afather](#note16a), though Abraham [bbe ignorant](#note16b) of us, and Israel acknowledge us not: thou, O Lord, art our father, our redeemer; thy name is from [ceverlasting](#note16c).

17 ¶ O Lord, why hast thou [amade](#note17a) us to err from thy ways, and [bhardened](#note17b) our heart from thy fear? Return for thy servants’ sake, the tribes of thine inheritance.

18 The [apeople](#note18a) of thy holiness have possessed it but a little while: our adversaries have [btrodden](#note18b) down thy sanctuary.

19 We are thine: thou never barest rule over them; they were not called by thy [aname](#note19a).

Chapter 64

The people of the Lord pray for the Second Coming and for the salvation that will then be theirs.

1 Oh that thou wouldest [arend](#note1a) the heavens, that thou wouldest come down, that the [bmountains](#note1b) might flow down at thy [cpresence](#note1c),

2 As when the melting fire burneth, the fire causeth the waters to boil, to make thy name known to thine adversaries, that the nations may [atremble](#note2a) at thy presence!

3 When thou didst [aterrible](#note3a) things which we looked not for, thou camest down, the [bmountains](#note3b) flowed down at thy presence.

4 For since the beginning of the world men have not heard, nor perceived by the ear, neither hath the [aeye](#note4a) seen, O God, beside thee, what he hath [bprepared](#note4b) for him that waiteth for him.

5 Thou meetest him that rejoiceth and worketh righteousness, those that remember thee in thy ways: behold, thou art wroth; for we have sinned: in those is continuance, and we shall be saved.

6 But we are all as an [aunclean thing](#note6a), and all our righteousnesses are as [bfilthy](#note6b) rags; and we all do fade as a leaf; and our iniquities, like the wind, have taken us away.

7 And there is none that calleth upon thy name, that stirreth up himself to take hold of thee: for thou hast hid thy [aface](#note7a) from us, and hast consumed us, because of our iniquities.

8 But now, O Lord, thou art our [afather](#note8a); we are the clay, and thou our potter; and we all are the [bwork](#note8b) of thy hand.

9 ¶ Be not wroth very sore, O Lord, neither remember iniquity for ever: behold, see, we beseech thee, we are all thy [apeople](#note9a).

10 Thy holy cities are a wilderness, Zion is a wilderness, Jerusalem a desolation.

11 Our holy and our [abeautiful](#note11a) house, where our fathers praised thee, is [bburned](#note11b) up with fire: and all our pleasant things are laid [cwaste](#note11c).

12 Wilt thou [arefrain](#note12a) thyself for these things, O Lord? wilt thou hold thy peace, and afflict us very sore?

Chapter 65

Ancient Israel was rejected for rejecting the Lord—The Lord’s people will rejoice and triumph during the Millennium.

1 I am [asought](#note1a) of them that asked not for me; I am found of them that sought me not: I said, Behold me, behold me, unto a nation that was not called by my [bname](#note1b).

2 I have spread out my hands all the day unto a [arebellious](#note2a) people, which walketh in a way that was not good, after their own thoughts;

3 A people that provoketh me to [aanger](#note3a) continually to my face; that sacrificeth in gardens, and burneth incense upon altars of [bbrick](#note3b);

4 [aWhich remain](#note4a) among the graves, and lodge in the monuments, which eat swine’s flesh, and broth of abominable things is in their vessels;

5 Which say, Stand by thyself, come not near to me; for I am [aholier](#note5a) than thou. These are a smoke in my nose, a fire that burneth all the day.

6 Behold, it is written before me: I will not keep silence, but will [arecompense](#note6a), even recompense into their bosom,

7 Your iniquities, and the iniquities of your fathers together, saith the Lord, which have burned incense upon the mountains, and [ablasphemed](#note7a) me upon the hills: therefore will I measure their former work into their bosom.

8 ¶ Thus saith the Lord, As the [anew wine](#note8a) is found in the cluster, and one saith, Destroy it not; for a blessing is in it: so will I do for my servants’ sakes, that I may [bnot](#note8b) destroy them all.

9 And I will bring forth a seed out of Jacob, and out of [aJudah](#note9a) an inheritor of my mountains: and mine [belect](#note9b) shall [cinherit](#note9c) it, and my servants shall dwell there.

10 And Sharon shall be a fold of flocks, and the valley of [aAchor](#note10a) a place for the herds to lie down in, for my people that have sought me.

11 ¶ But ye are they that forsake the Lord, that forget my holy mountain, that prepare a table for that [atroop](#note11a), and that furnish the drink offering unto that [bnumber](#note11b).

12 Therefore will I number you to the sword, and ye shall all bow down to the slaughter: because when I [acalled](#note12a), ye did not answer; when I spake, ye did not hear; but did evil before mine eyes, and did choose that wherein I delighted not.

13 Therefore thus saith the Lord God, Behold, my servants shall eat, but ye shall be hungry: behold, my servants shall drink, but ye shall be thirsty: behold, my servants shall rejoice, but ye shall be ashamed:

14 Behold, my servants shall sing for joy of heart, but ye shall cry for sorrow of heart, and shall [ahowl](#note14a) for vexation of spirit.

15 And ye shall leave your name for a [acurse](#note15a) unto my chosen: for the Lord God shall slay thee, and call his servants by another [bname](#note15b):

16 That he who [ablesseth himself](#note16a) in the earth shall bless himself in the God of truth; and he that sweareth in the earth shall [bswear](#note16b) by the God of truth; because the former troubles are forgotten, and because they are hid from mine eyes.

17 ¶ For, behold, I [acreate](#note17a) new [bheavens](#note17b) and a [cnew](#note17c) [dearth](#note17d): and the [eformer](#note17e) shall not be remembered, nor come into mind.

18 But be ye glad and rejoice for ever in that which I create: for, behold, I create Jerusalem a [arejoicing](#note18a), and her people a joy.

19 And I will [arejoice](#note19a) in Jerusalem, and joy in my people: and the voice of weeping shall be no more heard in her, nor the voice of crying.

20 There shall be no more thence an infant of days, nor an [aold](#note20a) man that hath not filled his days: for the [bchild](#note20b) shall die an hundred years old; but the sinner being an hundred years old shall be accursed.

21 And they shall build houses, and inhabit them; and they shall plant vineyards, and [aeat](#note21a) the fruit of them.

22 They shall not build, and another inhabit; they shall not plant, and another eat: for as the days of a [atree](#note22a) are the days of my people, and mine elect shall long enjoy the work of their hands.

23 They shall not [alabour](#note23a) in vain, nor bring forth for trouble; for they are the [bseed](#note23b) of the blessed of the Lord, and their [coffspring](#note23c) with them.

24 And it shall come to pass, that before they call, I will [aanswer](#note24a); and while they are yet speaking, I will hear.

25 The [awolf](#note25a) and the lamb shall [bfeed](#note25b) together, and the lion shall eat straw like the bullock: and dust shall be the serpent’s meat. They shall not [churt](#note25c) nor destroy in all my holy mountain, saith the Lord.
